Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Rububiyyah Acknowledged, Uluhiyyah Denied
Imam Ghazali shows polytheists knew Allah's Lordship but were disbelievers due to shirk in worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that acknowledging Allah as Creator and Sustainer (Tawhid ar-Rububiyyah) is not sufficient for Islam; one must also worship Him alone (Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah).

Core Idea
Knowing Allah's lordship is not enough; worship must be for Him alone.

Many people assume that believing in a Creator automatically makes one a believer. However, the Qur'an tells us that the polytheists of Makkah knew that Allah was the sole Creator, Provider, and Controller of the universe, yet they were not Muslims. In this passage, Imam Ghazali uses Quranic evidence to show that they were declared disbelievers because they associated partners in worship. This distinction between acknowledging lordship and practicing exclusive worship is a foundational concept in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the flow from verses to commentary to conclusion.
2
Identify the Quranic verses
The passage lists five verses (10:31, 43:87, 29:63, 27:62, 12:106). Read them and note what the polytheists acknowledged.
These verses establish their acknowledgment of Rububiyyah.
3
Understand Mujahid's interpretation
Imam Ghazali quotes Mujahid to clarify that their 'belief' was only verbal, coexisting with polytheistic practices.
This shows that their faith was incomplete.
4
Reflect on the ruling
The passage concludes that despite their knowledge and some acts of worship, their blood and property were permissible because of shirk in worship.
This highlights the gravity of violating Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بلازمه من توحيد الالهية ، لأن الله تعالى حكى عن المشركين أنهم مقرون بهذا التوحيد لله وحده : قال تعالى : قُلْ مَن يَرْزُقُكُم مِّنَ السَّمَاءِ وَالْأَرْضِ ، أَمَن يَمْلِكُ السَّمْعَ وَالْأَبْصَارَ، وَمَن يُخْرِجُ الْحَيَّ مِنَ الْمَيِّتِ وَيُخْرِجُ الْمَيِّتَ مِنَ الْحَيَّ ، وَمَن يُدَبِّرُ الْأَمْرَ فَسَيَقُولُونَ اللهُ ، فَقُلْ أَفَلَا تَتَّقُونَ ) (١) وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَلَئِن سَأَلْتَهُم مَّنْ خَلَقَهُمْ لَيَقُولُنَّ اللَّهُ ) (۲) وقال سبحانه: ﴿ وَلَئِن سَأَلْتَهُم مِّن نَّزَّلَ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً فَأَحْيَا بِهِ الْأَرْضَ مِن بَعْدِ مَوْتِهَا ، لَيَقُولُنَّ اللَّهُ ) (۳) وقال تعالى ( أَمَّن يُجِيبُ الْمُضْطَرَّ إِذَا دَعَاهُ وَيَكْشِفُ السُّوءَ وَيَجْعَلُكُمْ خُلَفَاءَ الْأَرْضِ ، أَإلهُ مَّعَ اللَّهِ قَلِيلًا مَّا تَذَكَّرُونَ ﴾ (٤) فكانوا يعلمون أن جميع ذلك لله وحده ، ولم يكونوا بذلك مسلمين ، بل قال تعالى : وَمَا يُؤْمِنُ أَكْثَرُهُم بالله إِلا وَهُم مُّشْرِكُونَ ) (٥) يقول مجاهد رضي الله عنه في معنى الآية : ايمانهم بالله قولهم : إنَّ الله خلقنا ويرزقنا ويميتنا ، فهذا إيمان مع شرك عبادتهم غيره فتبين أن الكفار يعرفون الله تعالى ويعرفون ربوبيته ، وملكه وقهره ، وكانوا مع ذلك يعبدونه ويخلصون له أنواعا من العبادات ، كالحج ، والصدقة ، والدعاء ، وقت الاضطرار ونحو ذلك ، ويدعون أنهم على ملة سيدنا ابراهيم عليه الصلاة والسلام ، فأنزل الله تعالى : مَا كَانَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ يَهُودِيًا وَلا نَصُرَانّياً ولَكن كَانَ حَنِيفاً مُسلِماً وَمَا كَانَ مِنَ المُشْرِكِينَ ) (١) . فكان بعضهم يؤمن بالبعث والحساب ، وبعضهم يؤمن بالقدر ، ومثل هذا كان يوجد في عقائدهم . فوجب على كل من عقل عن الله تعالى أن ينظر ويبحث عن السبب الذي أوجب سفك دمائهم ، ويسبي نسائهم ، وإباحة أموالهم ، مع هذا الإقرار والمعرفة ، وما ذاك إلا لاشراكهم في توحيد العبادة الذي هو معنى : « لا إله إلا الله " .
And its necessary consequence from the Tawhid of divinity, because Allah the Exalted related about the polytheists that they acknowledged this Tawhid for Allah alone. He said the Exalted: Say: 'Who provides for you from the heavens and the earth? Or who owns hearing and sight? And who brings forth the living from the dead and brings forth the dead from the living? And who disposes of the affairs?' They will say 'Allah.' Then say, 'Will you not then be righteous?' [10:31] And He said the Exalted: 'And if you ask them who created them, they will surely say Allah.' [43:87] And He the Exalted said: 'And if you ask them who sends down rain from the sky and revives the earth after its death, they will surely say Allah.' [29:63] And He said the Exalted: 'Or who answers the distressed when he calls upon Him, and removes the harm, and makes you successors on the earth? Is there a god with Allah? Little do you remember.' [27:62] They knew that all of that was for Allah alone, but they were not thereby Muslims. Rather, He said the Exalted: 'And most of them believe not in Allah except that they are polytheists.' [12:106] Mujahid, may Allah be pleased with him, said concerning the meaning of the verse: 'Their belief in Allah is their saying: "Indeed Allah created us, provides for us, and causes us to die." So this is belief along with polytheism.' Their worshipping other than Him became clear. So it became evident that the disbelievers know Allah the Exalted and know His lordship, His dominion, and His subjugation, and yet with that they worship Him and devote some types of worship to Him, such as Hajj, charity, supplication, times of distress, and the like. And they claimed they were upon the religion of our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him. So Allah the Exalted revealed: 'Ibrahim was neither a Jew nor a Christian, but he was a hanif, a Muslim, and he was not of the polytheists.' [3:67]. And some of them believed in resurrection and accountability, and some believed in predestination, and similar was found in their creeds. So it is incumbent upon everyone who understands from Allah the Exalted to consider and investigate the cause that necessitated the shedding of their blood, the captivity of their women, and the permissibility of their wealth, despite this acknowledgment and knowledge. And that was only due to their association of partners in the Tawhid of worship, which is the meaning of 'La ilaha illa Allah'.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a proof and explanation that the polytheists of the Quraysh acknowledged Tawhid ar-Rububiyyah (Oneness of Lordship) but were not considered Muslims because they violated Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah (Oneness of Worship). Imam Ghazali begins by stating that the necessary consequence of Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah (which was discussed before) is that the polytheists actually recognized this type of Tawhid for Allah alone. He then cites five Quranic verses (10:31, 43:87, 29:63, 27:62, 12:106) as evidence that the polytheists, when asked about creation, provision, and control, would attribute these to Allah. Yet they were not Muslims because they committed shirk in worship, as indicated in verse 12:106. Imam Ghazali then quotes the interpretation of Mujahid, who explains that their 'belief' (iman) was merely verbal acknowledgment that Allah is the Creator, Provider, and Giver of life and death, but this belief coexisted with their shirk. The text elaborates that the disbelievers in fact did know Allah's lordship, dominion, and subjugation, and they even performed some acts of worship like Hajj, charity, and supplication during distress, and claimed to follow the religion of Ibrahim. But Allah revealed that Ibrahim was not a polytheist and that their claim was false. Additionally, some of them believed in resurrection and predestination. Despite all this spiritual insight and practice, the Islamic ruling was that their blood, property, and families were permissible because of their shirk in worship. The lesson concludes that the true cause for their being fought was their shirk in Tawhid al-‘Ibadah, which is the meaning of 'La ilaha illa Allah'. This emphasizes that merely acknowledging Allah's Lordship is not sufficient; one must also dedicate worship exclusively to Him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that believing in Allah as Creator and Sustainer alone makes one a Muslim.
Correction: This passage shows that true Tawhid also requires exclusive worship of Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the reason for the permissibility of shedding the blood of the polytheists despite their acknowledgment of Allah's lordship and some acts of worship?
A) They denied the existence of Allah.
B) They associated partners in the Tawhid of worship.
C) They did not believe in the Hereafter.
D) They refused to perform Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Acknowledging Allah as Creator is not enough; one must worship Him alone, which is the core of 'La ilaha illa Allah'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You acknowledge that Allah is your Creator and Provider, but where in your life do you still place your hope or fear in created beings more than in Him? What specific act of reliance do you need to redirect to Allah alone today?
?
The polytheists performed Hajj, gave charity, and prayed during distress—yet they were still disbelievers. Are there any acts of worship you do that are tainted by showing off (riya) or seeking people's approval? How will you purify your intention in your next prayer?
?
If your faith is merely intellectual assent that Allah exists, but your heart and actions do not reflect exclusive devotion to Him, are you any better than the polytheists of Quraysh? What one change will you make this week to ensure your worship is for Allah alone?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

The Third Type: Tawheed of Worship (Uluhiyyah)
Defines Tawheed al-Uluhiyyah and its components with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of Tawheed al-Uluhiyyah and that it requires dedicating all inner states and outer acts of worship exclusively to Allah.

Core Idea
Tawheed of Worship is the call to direct every inner and outer act of devotion to Allah alone.

Having established Tawheed of Lordship and Tawheed of Names and Attributes, Imam al-Ghazali now presents the third and most practical type: Tawheed of Worship (al-Uluhiyyah). This is the tawheed that every believer lives out through love, fear, hope, trust, and all acts of worship. The following passage defines it and grounds it in two powerful Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how the author defines this tawheed through a list of devotional acts.
The Arabic term 'إخلاص التأله' is key—it means purifying one's devotion.
2
Identify the components of devotion
The passage lists several inner and outer acts: love, fear, hope, trust, desire, awe, and supplication. Ask yourself why each of these must be for Allah alone.
These are not just rituals; they are heart-based states.
3
Understand the scope of worship
The passage extends sincerity to all acts of worship, both apparent and hidden, and emphasizes that nothing—not even for angels or prophets—should be shared with Allah.
This includes actions like prayer, charity, and reliance.
4
Reflect on the Quranic verses
The two verses (al-Fatihah 5 and Hud 123) serve as proof texts. Consider how they capture the essence of this tawheed: worship and reliance solely on Allah.
The first verse is recited daily in every rak'ah of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتوحيد الالهية مبنى على إخلاص التأله الله تعالى من المحبة ، والخوف والرجاء ، والتوكل ، والرغبة ، والرهبة ، والدعاء الله وحده : وينبني على ذلك إخلاص العبادات كلها ظاهرها وباطنها الله وحده لا شريك له ، لا يجعل فيها شيئا لغيره ، لا لملك مقرب ، ولا لنبي مرسل ، فضلا عن غيرهما وهذا التوحيد هو الذي تضمنه قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِيَّاكَ نَعْبُدُ وَإِيَّاكَ نَسْتَعِينُ ) وقوله تعالى : ﴿فَاعْبُدْهُ وَتَوَكَّل عَلَيْهِ وَمَا رَبُّكَ بِغَافِلٍ عَمَّا تَعْمَلُونَ )
And Tawheed of Worship (al-Uluhiyyah) is based on sincere devotion to Allah Almighty in love, fear, hope, trust, desire, awe, and supplication to Allah alone. And upon that is based the sincerity of all acts of worship, both outward and inward, to Allah alone, without any partner; nothing of it is made for other than Him, not for a close angel nor for a sent prophet, let alone others. And this tawheed is what is encompassed by His statement: 'You alone we worship and You alone we ask for help' and His statement: 'So worship Him and rely upon Him. And your Lord is not unaware of what you do.'
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage defines the third and most crucial type of tawheed: 'Tawheed of Worship' (al-Uluhiyyah). The author explains that this tawheed is built upon purifying one's devotion (ikhlas al-ta'alluh) for Allah alone. He lists specific inward and outward acts: love (mahabbah), fear (khawf), hope (raja'), trust (tawakkul), desire (raghbah), awe (rahbah), and supplication (du'a). All these must be directed exclusively to Allah. From this foundational sincerity, the author states that all acts of worship, both apparent (like prayer, fasting) and hidden (like intentions, reliance), must be exclusively for Allah, with no partners — not even for the highest angels or prophets, let alone any other being. He then cites two Quranic verses: Surah al-Fatihah verse 5, 'You alone we worship and You alone we ask for help,' and Surah Hud verse 123, 'So worship Him and rely upon Him. And your Lord is not unaware of what you do.' These verses encapsulate the essence of tawheed al-uluhiyyah: directing worship and reliance to Allah alone.

Key Terms
توحيد الألوهية
إخلاص التأله
المحبة
الخوف
الرجاء
التوكل
الدعاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that Tawheed al-Uluhiyyah is only about verbal declarations or outward rituals, ignoring the inner states of the heart.
Correction: This passage shows that Tawheed al-Uluhiyyah begins with sincere devotion in the heart—including love, fear, hope, trust—and that these inner states must be directed solely to Allah, not just outward actions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of Tawheed al-Uluhiyyah?
A) Believing in Allah's names and attributes
B) Sincere devotion to Allah in love, fear, hope, and supplication
C) Performing the five pillars of Islam
D) Following the Prophet's sunnah

Key Takeaway
Tawheed al-Uluhiyyah requires that all inner states and outer acts of worship be devoted exclusively to Allah alone, as affirmed by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you offer supplication in times of need, do you ever find yourself calling upon anyone other than Allah, even a prophet or a righteous person? How does this passage confront you with the necessity of purifying that act?
?
Examine your heart: Is there anyone whose approval you fear losing more than Allah’s displeasure? How does the list of inner acts (love, fear, hope, trust, desire, awe) force you to recalibrate your deepest attachments?
?
Consider your daily routines: Is there any act of worship, whether apparent like prayer or hidden like intention, that you perform for the sake of someone else’s praise? How does the concept of 'ikhlāṣ al-ta'alluh' demand a complete reorientation of your intentions today?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
The Centrality of Tawhid and the Meaning of 'Ilah'
Ghazali defines Tawhid as the core of faith and explains the meaning of 'ilah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Tawhid is the essence of Islam and that the word 'ilah' signifies the one who is worshipped with love, fear, and reverence.

Core Idea
Tawhid is the first and last of the religion; 'ilah' means the One worshipped with all forms of devotion.

Ghazali opens this section by quoting several Quranic verses that command reliance and worship of Allah alone. He then declares that this Tawhid is the beginning and end of the religion, and explains the meaning of the testimony of faith by defining 'ilah' as the one who is worshipped with love, fear, and exaltation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Read the opening verses slowly, noting how each emphasizes reliance on Allah and worship of Him alone.
These verses set the foundation for the definition of Tawhid.
2
Identify the central claim
Find where Ghazali says 'This Tawhid is the first and last of the religion' and note how he ties it to the kalima.
3
Understand the definition of 'ilah'
Read Ghazali's definition of 'ilah' as the one worshipped with love, fear, reverence, and all types of worship. Reflect on why this is important.
This guards against reducing Tawhid to a mere verbal declaration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله سبحانه : ( فَإِن تَوَلُّوا فَقُلْ حَسْبِيَ اللهُ لا إلهَ إِلا هُوَ عَلَيْهِ تَوَكَّلْتُ وَهُوَ رَبُّ الْعَرْشِ الْعَظِيمِ ) . وقوله تعالى : ﴿ رَّبُّ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا فَاعْبُدْهُ وَاصْطَبِرْ لِعِبَادَتِهِ هَلْ تَعْلَمُ لَهُ سَمِيًّا ﴾ . وقوله سبحانه : ﴿ عَلَيْهِ تَوَكَّلْتُ وَإِلَيْهِ أُنِيبُ ﴾ . وقوله تعالى : ( وَتَوَكَّل عَلَى الْحَيِّ الَّذِي لَا يَمُوتُ وَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِهِ وَكَفَى بِهِ بِذُنُوبِ عِبَادِهِ خَبِيراً ) . وقوله سبحانه: ﴿ وَاعْبُدْ رَبَّكَ حَتَّى يَأْتِيَكَ الْيَقِينُ ﴾ . وهذا التوحيد هو أول الدين وآخره ، وباطنه وظاهره ، وهو أول دعوة الرسل وآخرها ، وهو معنى قول : لا إله إلا الله فإن الإله هو المألوه المعبود بالمحبة ، والخشية ، والإجلال والتعظيم ، وجميع أنواع العبادة ، ولأجل هذا التوحيد ، خلقت الخليقة ، وأرسلت الرسل ، وأنزلت الكتب ، وبه افترق الناس إلى مؤمنين ، وكفار ، وسعداء أهل الجنة ، وأشقياء أهل النار ، قال تعالى : يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ اعْبُدُوا رَبَّكُمُ الَّذِي خَلَقَكُمْ وَالَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكُمْ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَتَّقُونَ . فهذا أول أمر في القرآن الكريم . وقال سبحانه : وَلَقَدْ أَرْسَلْنَا نُوحاً إِلَى قَوْمِهِ فَقَالَ يَا قَوْمِ اعْبُدُوا اللهَ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرُهُ فهذا دعوة أول رسول بعد حدوث الشرك . وقال هود لقومه : ( اعْبُدُوا اللهَ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرُهُ ) . وقال صالح لقومه : ( اعْبُدُوا اللهَ مَا لَكُم مِّنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرُهُ ) . وقال شعيب لقومه : ( اعْبُدُوا اللهَ مَا لَكُمْ مِنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرُهُ ) . وقال إبراهيم عليه السلام لقومه : إِنِّي وَجَّهْتُ وَجْهِيَ لِلَّذِي فَطَرَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ حَنِيفاً وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ . وقال تعالى : ( وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ مِن رَّسُولٍ إِلَّا نُوحِي إِلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا أَنَا فَاعْبُدُونِ ) . وقال تعالى : ( وَاسْأَلْ مَنْ أَرْسَلْنَا مِن قَبْلِكَ مِن رُسُلِنَا أَجَعَلْنَا مِن دُونِ الرَّحْمَنِ آلِهَةً يُعْبَدُونَ ) . وقال سبحانه : ( وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنْسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونِ ) .
And His saying, the Exalted: (But if they turn away, say: Sufficient for me is Allah; there is no deity except Him. Upon Him I have relied, and He is the Lord of the Great Throne.) And His saying, the Exalted: [Lord of the heavens and the earth and whatever is between them, so worship Him and be steadfast in His worship. Do you know of any similarity to Him?] And His saying, the Exalted: [Upon Him I have relied, and to Him I turn in repentance.] And His saying, the Exalted: (And rely upon the Living who does not die, and exalt [Him] with His praise. And sufficient is He to be, of the sins of His servants, Aware.) And His saying, the Exalted: [And worship your Lord until there comes to you the certainty (of death).] And this Tawhid is the first of the religion and its last, its inward and its outward, and it is the first call of the messengers and their last, and it is the meaning of the saying: 'There is no deity except Allah.' For the deity (al-ilah) is the one who is worshipped (al-ma'luh al-ma'bud) with love, fear, reverence, and exaltation, and all types of worship. And for the sake of this Tawhid, creation was created, messengers were sent, and books were revealed, and by it people are divided into believers and disbelievers, and the happy people of Paradise and the wretched people of the Fire. He, the Exalted, said: O mankind, worship your Lord who created you and those before you that you may become righteous. So this is the first command in the Noble Qur'an. And He, the Exalted, said: And indeed We sent Noah to his people, and he said: O my people, worship Allah; you have no deity other than Him. So this is the call of the first messenger after the occurrence of polytheism. And Hud said to his people: (Worship Allah; you have no deity other than Him.) And Salih said to his people: (Worship Allah; you have no deity other than Him.) And Shu'ayb said to his people: (Worship Allah; you have no deity other than Him.) And Abraham, peace be upon him, said to his people: Indeed, I have turned my face toward He who created the heavens and the earth, inclining toward truth, and I am not of the polytheists. And He, the Exalted, said: (And We sent not before you any messenger except We revealed to him that there is no deity except Me, so worship Me.) And He, the Exalted, said: (And ask those We sent before you of Our messengers: Have We made besides the Most Merciful deities to be worshipped?) And He, the Exalted, said: (And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me.)
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a proof-text argument establishing the centrality of Tawhid (the oneness of Allah) in Islam. It begins by citing several Quranic verses that command worship and reliance on Allah alone. Then, Ghazali states that this Tawhid is the first and last of the religion, its inward and outward, and the first and last call of the messengers. He explains the meaning of 'La ilaha illallah' by defining 'ilah' (deity) as the one who is worshipped with love, fear, reverence, exaltation, and all forms of worship. He emphasizes that for this Tawhid, creation, messengers, and books were sent, and it is the criterion by which people are divided into believers and disbelievers, Paradise and Fire. He then quotes verse 2:21 (O mankind, worship your Lord...) as the first command in the Qur'an. Continuing, Ghazali shows that all prophets—Noah, Hud, Salih, Shu'ayb, Abraham (peace be upon them)—called to the same message of worshipping Allah alone. He concludes with universal verses affirming that all messengers were sent with this message (21:25, 43:45) and that the purpose of creation is worship (51:56). The passage thus grounds the definition of Tawhid in both revelation and the consistent call of the prophets.

Key Terms

إله
عبادة
لا إله إلا الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that saying 'La ilaha illallah' is sufficient without internal states of love and fear.
Correction: Ghazali defines 'ilah' as the one worshipped with love, fear, and reverence, showing that Tawhid requires heartfelt devotion, not just utterance.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what does 'ilah' mean in the phrase 'La ilaha illallah'?
A) The Creator of the universe.
B) The one who is worshipped with love, fear, reverence, and all types of worship.
C) The one who has no partners in His divinity.
D) The one who sends messengers.

Key Takeaway
Tawhid is the foundation of Islam, and 'ilah' means the One who is worshipped with complete love, fear, and reverence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that Tawhid is the first and last of the religion. Is it the first and last of your daily concerns? What concrete change can you make tomorrow to put Tawhid at the center of your thoughts and actions?
?
Ghazali defines 'ilah' as the one worshipped with love and fear. When you examine your heart, which of these—love or fear—is weaker in your worship? What is one specific step you can take this week to strengthen that missing element?
?
The passage commands worship until certainty (death) arrives. If you knew you would die one year from today, what would change in how you worship? Why wait until certainty is imminent?

The Prophetic Call and the Purpose of Creation
Ghazali shows the universal call of Tawhid and the purpose of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all prophets called to the same message of worshipping Allah alone, and that the purpose of creation is the worship of Allah.

Core Idea
All prophets called to Tawhid, and the purpose of jinn and humans is to worship Allah alone.

After establishing the meaning of Tawhid, Ghazali demonstrates its universality. He shows that for Tawhid, creation was made, messengers were sent, and it is the criterion of belief. He then quotes the first command in the Quran (2:21) and the calls of various prophets, all inviting to worship Allah alone. The passage concludes with the explicit purpose of creation: worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the sentence 'For the sake of this Tawhid, creation was created...' and note the comprehensive role of Tawhid.
2
Examine the prophetic examples
Read the verses about Noah, Hud, Salih, Shu'ayb, and Abraham. Notice how each prophet's call is identical: 'Worship Allah; you have no deity other than Him.'
This shows the consistency of the message.
3
Consider the purpose of creation
Read the final verse (51:56) and reflect on its meaning: the purpose of jinn and mankind is to worship Allah.
This links the principle of Tawhid directly to human existence.

Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah: The First Obligation
Establishing Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah as the first obligation and listing its names

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah (the oneness of worship) is the first and foremost obligation in Islam and how the Qur'an consistently emphasizes it.

Core Idea
The first call of every prophet is to worship Allah alone.

This passage from Imam al-Ghazali's Qawa'id al-'Aqa'id establishes Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah as the central and primary duty of every accountable person. Drawing on prophetic traditions and Qur'anic verses, it clarifies that the testimony of 'la ilaha illa Allah' is the first and last obligation, and that the entire Qur'an revolves around this principle. Let's explore the textual evidence and the various names given to this fundamental Tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the English translation. Notice how the flow moves from hadith narratives to doctrinal statements to Qur'anic proofs.
2
Identify the key claim about the first obligation
Find where the author states that Tawhid is the first obligation. What views does he reject? Understand why reflection (nazar) and doubt are not the first duty.
The author explicitly rejects those who say reflection or doubt is the first duty.
3
List the names of this Tawhid
The passage gives several names for this type of Tawhid. Identify them and understand their meanings: Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah, Tawhid al-Ibadah, Tawhid al-Iradah, Tawhid al-Qasd, Tawhid al-'Aml.
Each name highlights a different aspect: devotion, worship, intention, purpose, action.
4
Reflect on the Qur'anic evidence
Notice how the author uses verses from Surah al-Zumar and then argues that every surah and verse of the Qur'an points to this Tawhid. How does he categorize Qur'anic content to make this argument?
The author divides Qur'anic content into information about Allah (which implies this Tawhid) and direct commands to worship Him alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال هرقل لأبي سفيان لما سأله عن النبي ما يقول لكم؟ قال يقول: اعبدوا الله ولا تشركوا به شيئا، واتركوا ما يقول آباؤكم. وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم للمعاذ رضي الله عنه: إنك تأتي قوما أهل كتاب فليكن أول ما تدعوهم إليه شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله. وهذا التوحيد هو أول واجب على المكلف، لا النظر، ولا القصد إلى النظر، ولا الشك في الله، كما هي أقوال لمن لم يدر لما بعث الله به رسوله، من معاني الكتاب والحكمة. فهو أول واجب، وآخر واجب، وأول ما يدخل به الإسلام، وآخر ما يخرج به من الدنيا. وقد أفصح القرآن الكريم عن هذا النوع كل الإفصاح، وبدأ فيه وأعاد، وضرب لذلك الأمثال، بحيث أن كل سورة في القرآن فيها الدلالة على هذا التوحيد. ويسمى هذا النوع: توحيد الإلهية، لأنه مبني على إخلاص التأله، وهو أشد المحبة لله وحده، وذلك يستلزم إخلاص العبادة وحده. وتوحيد العبادة لذلك. وتوحيد الإرادة، لأنه مبني على إرادة وجه الله بالأعمال الصالحة. وتوحيد القصد، لأنه مبني على إخلاص القصد المستلزم لإخلاص العبادة لله. وتوحيد العمل، لأنه مبني على إخلاص العمل لله تعالى وحده. قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْبُدِ اللَّهَ مُخْلِصاً لَّهُ الدِّينَ﴾ (1) وقال سبحانه: ﴿قُلْ إِنِّي أُمِرْتُ أَنْ أَعْبُدَ اللهَ مُخْلِصاً لَّهُ الدِّينَ، وَأُمِرْتُ لِأَنْ أَكُونَ أَوَّلَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ﴾ (2). وقال تعالى: ﴿قُلِ اللَّهَ أَعْبُدُ مُخْلِصاً لَّهُ دِينِي فَاعْبُدُوا مَا شِئْتُم مِّن دُونِهِ﴾ (3) وقال سبحانه: ﴿قُلْ أَفَغَيْرَ اللَّهِ تَأْمُرُونِّي أَعْبُدُ أَيُّهَا الْجَاهِلُونَ، وَلَقَدْ أُوحِيَ إِلَيْكَ وَإِلَى الَّذِينَ مِن قَبْلِكَ لَئِنْ أَشْرَكْتَ لَيَحْبَطَنَّ عَمَلُكَ وَلَتَكُونَنَّ مِنَ الْخَاسِرِينَ، بَلِ اللَّهَ فَاعْبُدْ وَكُن مِّنَ الشَّاكِرِينَ﴾ (4). فكل هذه الآيات في الدعاء إلى هذا التوحيد، والأمر به، والجواب عن الشبهات والمعارضات، وذكر ما أعد الله لأهله من النعيم المقيم، وما أعد لمن خالفه من العذاب الأليم. وكل سورة في القرآن الكريم، بل وكل آية في القرآن، فهي داعية إلى هذا التوحيد، شاهدة به، متضمنة له. لأن القرآن الكريم، إما خبر عن الله تعالى وأسمائه وصفاته وأفعاله، وهو توحيد الربوبية وتوحيد الصفات، فذاك مستلزم لهذا متضمن له. وأما دعاء إلى عبادته وحده لا شريك له، وخلع ما يعبد من دونه أو أمر.
And Heraclius said to Abu Sufyan when he asked him about the Prophet: What does he say to you? He said: He says: Worship Allah and do not associate anything with Him, and abandon what your fathers say. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to Mu'adh, may Allah be pleased with him: You are going to a people of the Book, so let the first thing you call them to be the testimony that there is no god but Allah. And this Tawhid is the first obligation upon the accountable person, not reflection, nor the intention to reflect, nor doubt about Allah, as are the sayings of those who have not understood what Allah sent His Messenger with from the meanings of the Book and wisdom. So it is the first obligation and the last obligation, and the first thing by which one enters Islam and the last thing by which one leaves the world. And the Noble Qur'an has fully elucidated this type, began and repeated it, and struck examples for it, such that every surah in the Qur'an contains evidence for this Tawhid. And this type is called: Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah, because it is built on sincerity of devotion, and it is the most intense love for Allah alone, and that entails sincerity of worship alone. And Tawhid al-Ibadah is for that reason. And Tawhid al-Iradah, because it is built on desiring the face of Allah through righteous deeds. And Tawhid al-Qasd, because it is built on sincerity of intention which entails sincerity of worship to Allah. And Tawhid al-'Aml, because it is built on sincerity of action for Allah alone. Allah Almighty said: 'So worship Allah, making the religion pure for Him' (1). And He, exalted, said: 'Say: Indeed I am commanded to worship Allah, making the religion pure for Him, and I am commanded to be the first of the Muslims' (2). And He, exalted, said: 'Say: Allah I worship, making my religion pure for Him, so worship what you will besides Him' (3). And He, exalted, said: 'Say: Do you order me to worship other than Allah, O ignorant ones? And it has been revealed to you and to those before you: If you associate partners, your deeds will surely come to nothing and you will surely be among the losers. Rather, worship Allah and be among the grateful' (4). So all these verses are for calling to this Tawhid, commanding it, responding to doubts and objections, and mentioning what Allah has prepared for its people of everlasting bliss and what He has prepared for those who oppose it of painful punishment. And every surah in the Noble Qur'an, indeed every verse in the Qur'an, is a caller to this Tawhid, a witness to it, and inclusive of it. Because the Noble Qur'an is either informing about Allah Almighty, His names, attributes, and actions—which is Tawhid al-Rububiyyah and Tawhid al-Sifat—and that entails and includes this. Or it is a call to worship Him alone with no partner, and to abandon what is worshipped besides Him, or a command.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage establishes the centrality and primacy of Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah (the oneness of worship) in Islamic doctrine. It begins with a historical narrative from the hadith of Heraclius and the instruction to Mu'adh (may Allah be pleased with him) that the first call should be to the shahada, 'la ilaha illa Allah.' The author then declares that this Tawhid is the first and last obligation upon the accountable person (mukallaf), rejecting alternative views that place reflection (nazar) or doubt as the first duty. He emphasizes that the Qur'an fully clarifies this type of Tawhid, and every surah contains evidence for it. The passage then defines the names of this Tawhid: Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah (based on sincere devotion and intense love for Allah), Tawhid al-Ibadah (worship), Tawhid al-Iradah (intention for Allah's face), Tawhid al-Qasd (sincerity of purpose), and Tawhid al-'Aml (sincerity of action). To support this, the author quotes four verses from Surah al-Zumar (39:2, 11-12, 14-15, 64-66) that command sincere worship and warn against associating partners. He then concludes that all these verses call to this Tawhid and address doubts. Furthermore, every surah and verse of the Qur'an either informs about Allah's names, attributes, and actions (which is Tawhid al-Rububiyyah and al-Sifat) and necessarily implies Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah, or it directly commands worship of Allah alone and abandonment of false deities. Thus the entire Qur'an is a witness to and inclusive of this fundamental Tawhid.

Key Terms
توحيد الإلهية (Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah)
توحيد العبادة (Tawhid al-Ibadah)
توحيد الإرادة (Tawhid al-Iradah)
توحيد القصد (Tawhid al-Qasd)
توحيد العمل (Tawhid al-'Aml)
توحيد الربوبية (Tawhid al-Rububiyyah)
توحيد الصفات (Tawhid al-Sifat)
المكلف (al-mukallaf - the accountable person)
النظر (al-nazar - reflection)
شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله (shahada)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The first obligation upon a mukallaf is reflection (nazar) or doubt about God's existence.
Correction: The first obligation is the testimony of Tawhid (la ilaha illa Allah), as established by the Prophet's practice and the Qur'an.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the first obligation upon the accountable person?
A) Reflection (nazar) on the created world
B) Doubt (shakk) about God's existence
C) The testimony of Tawhid (shahada)
D) Intending to reflect (qasd ila al-nazar)

Key Takeaway
Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah is the core message of every prophet and the central theme of the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you actively seek to understand how each surah calls you to worship Allah alone, or do you recite without this awareness? What would change if you approached every verse as a direct command to purify your worship?
?
The author states that Tawhid is the first and last obligation, the entrance to Islam and the exit from the world. Have you ever examined whether your own entrance into Islam was based on this Tawhid, or on something else? Are you living your life with this as your final exit?
?
The passage describes Tawhid al-Uluhiyyah as built on the most intense love for Allah alone. When you examine your heart, what other loves compete with your love for Allah? Are you willing to abandon them as the first call demands? What specific step will you take today to make your love for Allah supreme?

The Positive Content of the Shahada: Tawhid and Risala
Ghazali enumerates what the shahada includes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the testimony of faith includes complete belief in Allah from the aspects of lordship and divinity, and that the testimony to the Prophet includes belief in angels, books, messengers, the Last Day, and the principles of Sharia.

Core Idea
The shahada is the foundation of a complete belief system, not just a phrase.

Ghazali begins by explaining the full implications of the two parts of the shahada. The first part requires belief in Allah's oneness, lordship, and divinity. The second part necessitates belief in all that the Prophet brought: angels, scriptures, messengers, the afterlife, and Islamic law. This passage shows that the shahada is the foundation of a complete belief system.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the shahada's positive content
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Ghazali structures the two parts of the shahada.
Pay attention to the Quranic verse cited.
2
Identify the two parts and their components
The first part (tawhid) includes rububiyya and uluhiyya. The second part (risala) includes belief in angels, books, messengers, Last Day, and Sharia principles.
3
Reflect on the comprehensiveness
Why does Ghazali emphasize that the shahada implies all these beliefs? What would be missing if someone only said the words without conviction?
This connects to the learning objective.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتجرى عليه أحكامه. فالشهادة بوحدانية الله سبحانه تتضمن كمال العقيدة في الله من جهتي الربوبية (الخلق والتربية) والألوهية (العبادة). والشهادة برسالة سيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم تتضمن التصديق بكمال العقيدة في الملائكة، والكتب، والرسل، واليوم الآخر، وأصول الشريعة والأحكام: آمن الرسول بما أنزل إليه من ربه والمؤمنون، كل آمن بالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله، لا نفرق بين أحد من رسله. فمن لم يؤمن بوجود الله سبحانه، أو لم يؤمن بوحدانيته تعالى، وتنزهه عن المشابهة، والحلول والاتحاد، أو لم يؤمن بتفرده بتدبير الكون والتصرف فيه، واستحقاق العبادة والتقديس، واستباح عبادة مخلوق ما من المخلوقات، لم يؤمن بأن الله رسالات إلى خلقه، بعث بها رسله صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم، وأنزل عليهم كتبه عن طريق ملائكته، أو لم يؤمن بما تضمنته الكتب من الرسل، أو فرق بين الرسل الذين قص علينا، فآمن بالبعض وكفر بالبعض، أو لم يؤمن بأن الحياة الدنيا تفنى ويعقبها دار أخرى هي ودار الاقامة الأبدية، بل اعتقد أن الحياة الدنيا حياة دائمة لا الجزاء [؟] دار تنقطع، أو اعتقد أنها تفنى فناء دائما لا بعث بعده، ولا حساب ولا جزاء، أو لم يؤمن بأن أصول شرع الله تعالى فيما حرم، وفيما أوجب، هي دينه القويم الذي يجب أن يتبع، فحرم من تلقاء نفسه ما رأى تحريمه، وأوجب من تلقاء نفسه ما رأى وجوبه. من لم يؤمن بجانب من هذه الحقائق لا يكون مسلما، ولا تجرى عليه أحكام المسلمين.
And its rulings apply to him. So the testimony to the oneness of Allah, exalted is He, includes complete belief in Allah from the two aspects of lordship (creation and nurturing) and divinity (worship). And the testimony to the mission of our master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, includes affirmation of complete belief in the angels, the books, the messengers, the Last Day, and the principles of the Sharia and rulings: 'The Messenger believes in what has been revealed to him from his Lord, and the believers; each believes in Allah, His angels, His books, and His messengers, saying we do not differentiate between any of His messengers.' So whoever does not believe in the existence of Allah, exalted is He, or does not believe in His oneness, His transcendence above resemblance, indwelling, and union, or does not believe in His uniqueness in managing the universe and disposing of it, and His deserving worship and sanctification, and deems permissible the worship of any created being among the creatures, does not believe that Allah sent messages to His creation, sent His messengers with them, and revealed His books to them through His angels, or does not believe in what the books contain of the messengers, or differentiates between the messengers whom He told us about, believing in some and disbelieving in others, or does not believe that this worldly life perishes and is followed by another abode which is the eternal dwelling place, but rather believes that this worldly life is a permanent life that does not cease [with?] reward [or] abode, or believes that it perishes permanently with no resurrection after it, no account, and no recompense, or does not believe that the principles of Allah's law regarding what He prohibited and what He obligated are His straight religion which must be followed, so he prohibits on his own accord what he sees as prohibited, and obligates on his own accord what he sees as obligatory. Whoever does not believe in any aspect of these truths is not a Muslim, and the rulings of Muslims do not apply to him.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of what the testimony of faith entails, Ghazali explains that the shahada to Allah's oneness includes perfect belief in Allah from two angles: lordship (rububiyya) which encompasses creation and nurturing, and divinity (uluhiyya) which demands worship. Similarly, the shahada to the Prophet's mission includes belief in angels, books, messengers, the Last Day, and the fundamentals of Sharia, as indicated by the Quranic verse. Then Ghazali lists the negations: if anyone denies any of these — such as God's existence, oneness, transcendence, unique management of the universe, or the message, or differentiates between prophets, or denies the afterlife, or rejects the authority of Sharia — such a person is not a Muslim and Islamic rulings do not apply to them. The passage thus demonstrates that Islamic faith is a comprehensive system; rejecting even one component nullifies one's Islam.

كمال العقيدة

Correction: Ghazali shows it implies full conviction in all fundamentals.

The shahada commits a Muslim to a complete set of beliefs about Allah, prophethood, the unseen, and divine law; it is not an empty phrase.

What Negates the Shahada: Denial of Any Fundamental
Ghazali enumerates beliefs whose denial nullifies faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that denying any fundamental aspect of Islamic belief—such as God's oneness, prophethood, the afterlife, or the authority of Sharia—negates one's testimony of faith and removes one from Islam.

Core Idea
Faith is all or nothing; rejecting one pillar nullifies the whole.

After establishing what the shahada includes, Ghazali turns to its inverse: what invalidates it. He lists a series of denials that, if held, mean a person is not a Muslim. This underscores the interconnectedness of Islamic beliefs—each essential component is necessary for valid faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage listing the negations
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the repeated phrase 'or does not believe' which introduces each denial.
2
Identify the specific denials mentioned
Make a mental list: denial of God's existence, oneness, transcendence, unique management, worship of other than God, denial of messages, differentiation between prophets, denial of afterlife, denial of Sharia authority.
There are nine distinct denials.
3
Understand the consequence
Ghazali concludes that whoever denies any of these is not a Muslim and Islamic rulings do not apply. This shows the absolute necessity of every article of faith.
Reflect on how this relates to the positive content from the previous lesson.

Three States of Belief According to Ghazali
Ghazali enumerates three states of belief, defining the first two fully and beginning the third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's classification of believers into three states based on the completeness and basis of their belief, focusing on the first two states.

Core Idea
Belief can be complete or partial, based on imitation or evidence.

Imam al-Ghazali provides a nuanced classification of people's belief. He distinguishes between believing all pillars through imitation versus believing only some pillars while ignoring others. This passage introduces the first two states and begins the third, setting the stage for a deeper discussion of what constitutes sound faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the three states Ghazali enumerates.
Notice that the third state is cut off mid-sentence.
2
Analyze the first state
Focus on the first state: belief in all pillars through imitation (taqlid). Ask yourself why Ghazali considers this a distinct category.
Imitation here means accepting faith without personal verification.
3
Analyze the second state
Examine the second state: belief in only some pillars, with no opinion on the remaining attributes. Consider the example given (existence and life only).
Ghazali questions whether such a person is a believer or merely a Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما بالنسبة لأهل الاعتقاد فإن للإمام الغزالي رضي الله عنه كلام نفيس يقول فيه: أن أهل الاعتقاد المجرد تحصينه بالعلم وتوثيقه بالأدلة، ينقسمون من وجه على ثلاث حالات: الأولى: أن يعتقد أحدهم جميع أركان الإيمان على ما يكمل عليه في الغالب، لكنه على طريق التقليد. الثانية: أن لا يعتقد إلا بعض الأركان مما فيه خلاف إذا انفرد ولم ينصف إليه في اعتقاده سواه، هل يكون به مؤمناً أو مسلما، مثل أن يعتقد وجود الواحد فقط، أو يعتقد أنه موجود حي لا غير، وأمثال هذه التقريرات، ويخلو عن اعتقاد باقي المصنفات خلواً كاملاً لا يعتقد فيها حقاً ولا باطلاً. الثالثة: أن يعتقد الوجود كما قلناه، أو الوجود والوحدانية، والحياة
As for the people of belief, al-Imam al-Ghazali, may Allah be pleased with him, has a precious statement. He says: The people of mere belief, its fortification with knowledge and its confirmation with proofs, are divided from one aspect into three states: The first: that one of them believes in all the pillars of faith in the manner that is generally sufficient, but it is by way of imitation (taqlid). The second: that he believes only some of the pillars concerning which there is disagreement, if isolated and nothing else is added to his belief—whether such a person is a believer or a Muslim, such as believing in the existence of the One only, or believing that He exists, living, and nothing else, and similar affirmations, and is completely devoid of belief in the remaining attributes, not believing in them as true or false. The third: that he believes in existence as we have said, or existence and oneness, and life...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents a classification by Imam al-Ghazali. He divides people who have mere belief (without deeper knowledge) into three states. The first state is one where a person believes all the pillars of faith in a way that is generally sufficient, but this belief is based on imitation (taqlid) rather than independent evidence. The second state is where a person believes only some of the pillars, particularly those that are disputed (such as believing in God's existence only, or that He exists and is living but nothing else), and has no belief at all in the remaining attributes—neither affirming nor denying them. The third state, which is cut off, begins to describe someone who believes in existence, or existence and oneness and life, but the description is incomplete. The passage thus highlights that not all belief is equally sound; belief based on imitation is acceptable to some degree, but partial belief or ignorance of attributes is problematic.

Key Terms
أهل الاعتقاد
التقليد
الأركان
المصنفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any belief, even if partial or without understanding, is sufficient for faith.
Correction: Ghazali shows that incomplete belief (e.g., believing only in God's existence and life, ignoring other attributes) is a deficient state that requires scrutiny. True faith should encompass all pillars and be based on knowledge or at least comprehensive imitation.

Checkpoint
In Ghazali's classification, what characterizes the second state of belief?
A) Full belief in all pillars through evidence
B) Belief in some pillars only, with no opinion on the rest
C) Denial of all pillars
D) Belief through imitation only

Key Takeaway
Ghazali distinguishes between comprehensive belief through imitation and partial belief without affirmation or denial of other attributes, showing that not all belief is equally valid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Faith and Disbelief

Ghazali's Three States of Belief
Ghazali classifies believers into three states regarding knowledge and belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's three-way classification of believers based on the extent and correctness of their belief in the pillars of faith.

Core Idea
Belief varies in completeness and correctness; not all believers are equal.

Imam al-Ghazali presents a nuanced view of belief among people who claim faith. He recognizes that mere belief is not uniform; it can be fortified by knowledge and proofs. In this passage, he divides such people into three categories, ranging from complete but imitative belief, to partial belief with ignorance, to belief with error. This classification helps us understand the spectrum of faith and its rulings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that Ghazali first introduces the division and then lists three states.
Pay attention to the keywords: تقليد, بدعة, كفر.
2
Identify the three states
List the three states described. For each, note what the person believes and what they lack.
3
Compare the second and third states
What is the key difference between state two (partial belief with ignorance) and state three (belief with error)? Ghazali says state three is bid'ah but not kufr.
4
Reflect on the implications
Why does Ghazali mention that there is disagreement about state two? How does this classification help in theological discussions about faith and disbelief?
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you can distinguish the three states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما بالنسبة لأهل الاعتقاد فإن للإمام الغزالي رضي الله عنه كلام نفيس يقول فيه : أن أهل الاعتقاد المجرد تحصينه بالعلم وتوثيقه بالأدلة ، ينقسمون من وجه على ثلاث حالات :
الأولى : أن يعتقد أحدهم جميع أركان الإيمان على ما يكمل عليه في الغالب ، لكنه على طريق التقليد
·
الثانية : أن لا يعتقد إلا بعض الأركان مما فيه خلاف إذا انفرد ولم ينصف إليه في اعتقاده سواه ، هل يكون به مؤمناً أو مسلما ، مثل أن يعتقد وجود الواحد فقط ، أو يعتقد أنه موجود حيى لاغير ، وأمثال هذه التقريرات ، ويخلو عن اعتقاد باقي الصفات خلوا كاملا لا يعتقد فيها حقا ولا باطلا
الثالثة : أن يعتقد الوجود كما قلناه ، أو الوجود والوحدانية ، والحياة ، وفي باقي الصفات على ما لا يوافق الحق بما هو بدعة أو ضلالة ، وليس بكفر صراح
As for the people of belief, Imam al-Ghazali, may Allah be pleased with him, has a precious statement. He says: Those who possess mere belief—fortifying it with knowledge and strengthening it with proofs—are divided, from one perspective, into three states:
First: That one believes all the pillars of faith according to what completes it in general, but by way of taqlid (imitation).
Second: That one believes only some of the pillars, concerning which there is disagreement if considered alone and nothing else is joined to it in one's belief—whether he is thereby a believer or a Muslim? For example, that he believes in the existence of the One only, or that he believes He exists, living, nothing else, and the like of these affirmations, and he is completely devoid of belief in the remaining attributes, not believing in them as true nor false.
Third: That he believes in existence as we said, or existence and oneness, and life, but regarding the remaining attributes (he believes) in what does not agree with the truth, being an innovation or misguidance, but not explicit disbelief.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a classification. Ghazali introduces a division of people who possess belief (i'tiqad) but seek to fortify it with knowledge and proofs. He divides them into three states based on the extent and correctness of their belief. The first state is a person who believes all the pillars of faith (arkan al-iman) in a complete manner, but their belief is based on taqlid (imitation) without personal investigation. The second state is a person who believes only some of the pillars—for example, only the existence of God or existence and life—and is completely ignorant of the remaining attributes, having neither true nor false belief about them. Ghazali notes that there is disagreement on whether such a person is a believer or Muslim. The third state is a person who believes in existence, oneness, and life, but holds incorrect beliefs about the remaining attributes (e.g., anthropomorphic or heretical views) that are bid'ah (innovation) or dhalalah (misguidance), but not outright kufr (disbelief). This classification shows that belief can vary in completeness and correctness, and Ghazali sets up a framework to discuss their rulings.

Key Terms
اعتقاد
تقليد
أركان الإيمان
بدعة
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That someone who lacks belief in any attribute is automatically a disbeliever.
Correction: Ghazali distinguishes between ignorance (state two) and false belief (state three); ignorance alone does not necessarily make one a disbeliever.

Checkpoint
In the second state, what does the person believe?
A) All pillars of faith but by taqlid.
B) Only existence and oneness, with correct belief about other attributes.
C) Only some pillars, e.g., existence, but is completely ignorant of the rest.
D) Existence, oneness, and life, but with heretical views on other attributes.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali's three states show that belief is not binary; it can be complete, partial, or erroneous, with different theological implications.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of Ghazali's three states best describes your own belief in Allah's attributes? Are you content with taqlid, or have you actively sought knowledge to fortify your faith? What will you do today to move toward a stronger state?
?
You may hold some correct beliefs, but consider: are there areas of your faith where you are entirely ignorant (like state two) or where you hold a position that might be incorrect (state three)? How will you seek the truth about those matters?
?
This lesson reveals that belief is not simply 'Muslim' or 'disbeliever'. Does this change how you view fellow Muslims who differ in their understanding of Allah's attributes? Will you now approach them with more patience and a desire to learn, rather than judging?

The Sufficiency of the Shahada for Islam
Ghazali defends the Islam of those with minimal belief using the shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that the shahada alone, with minimal belief in God's existence and oneness, is sufficient for one to be considered a Muslim, based on the practice of the Prophet and the early Salaf.

Core Idea
The shahada alone suffices for Islam, even without detailed knowledge of attributes.

In this passage, Imam al-Ghazali addresses a crucial question: what is the minimum belief required to be considered a Muslim? He defends the view that the simple declaration of faith (shahada) with heartfelt conviction in God's existence and oneness, and acceptance of the Prophet, is enough. This stance is grounded in the practice of the Prophet and the early Salaf, who did not require detailed theological knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Ghazali's own argument flow before you interpret.
Notice how Ghazali begins with a ruling, then addresses objections.
2
Identify the two states Ghazali distinguishes
Ghazali mentions 'the people of the first state' and 'the people of the second state'. Understand what each state refers to in terms of belief and knowledge.
The first state likely refers to those with complete belief by taqlid, the second to those with only minimal belief in existence.
3
Analyze the evidence from the Prophet and the Salaf
Ghazali cites the Prophet's acceptance of the shahada alone and the Salaf's silence on requiring more. Reflect on how this supports the argument.
This is the core of his defense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يدل عليه العلم ، ويستنبط من ظواهر الشرع، أن أرباب الحالة الأولى على سبيل نجاة ، ووصف ايمان واسلام ، وأما أهل الحالة الثانية : فالمتقدمون من السلف لم يشتهر عنهم في صورة هذه المسألة ، يخرج صاحب العقيدة عن حكم الإيمان والإسلام وجود الله تعالى ، والمتأخرون مختلفون ، وكثير خاف أن يخرج من اعتقاد واظهار الاقرار به ونبيه من الاسلام ، ولا يبعد أن يكون كثير ممن أسلم من الأجلاف والرعيات ، وضعفاء النساء والاتباع ، هذا عقده بلا مزيد عليه ولو سئلوا واستكشفوا عن الله عز وجل ، هل له ارادة ، أو كلام ، أو بقاء ، أو ما شاكل ذلك ؟ وهل له صفات معنوية ليست هي هو ، ولا هي غيره ، ربما وجدوا ويجهلون ذلك ولا يعقلون وجه ما يخاطبون به ، وكيف يخرج الله تعالى ، ووحدانيته تعالى ، مع الاقرار بالنبوة من حكم الإسلام ، والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد رفع القتال والقتل عنهم ، فأوجب حكم الإيمان والاسلام لمن قال : لا إله إلا الله ، وعقد عليها ، وهذه الكلمة لا تقتضى من اعتقد وجود أكثر من اعتقاد الوجود والوحدة في الظاهر ، وعلى البديهة من غير نظر ثم سمعنا عمن قالها في صدر الاسلام ولم يعلم بعدها الافرائض الوضوء والصلاة ، أو هو باق ببقاء ، أو بنفسه ، وأشباه هذه المعارف ولا يدفع ظهور هذا الا معاند أو جاهل بسيرة السلف ، وما جرى بينهم ، ويدل على قوة هذا الجانب في الشرع أن من استكشف منه على هذه ، الحالة وتحققت منه وأبي أن يذعن الى تعلم ما زاد على ما عنده ، لم يفت أحد
And what is indicated by knowledge and derived from the apparent meanings of the Shari'a is that the people of the first state are on the path of salvation and described with iman and islam. As for the people of the second state: the earlier of the Salaf did not become known from them regarding the form of this issue [that] the possessor of such a creed exits from the ruling of iman and islam due to (merely) believing in the existence of Allah Almighty? And the later ones differ, and many feared that one who believes [only in] existence and manifests acceptance of Him and His Prophet may exit from islam. And it is not unlikely that many of those who embraced Islam from among the rough [people], the commoners, the weak women, and the followers, their creed is this without addition. And if they were asked and examined about Allah Almighty: Does He have will, or speech, or everlastingness, or the like? And does He have attribute meaning that are not He nor other than He? Perhaps they would be found ignorant of that and not understand the manner of what they are addressed with. And how could one who believes in Allah Almighty and His oneness along with acceptance of prophethood exit from the ruling of islam? And the Prophet (peace be upon him) lifted from them fighting and killing, so he made the ruling of iman and islam obligatory for whoever says 'La ilaha illa Allah' and holds firmly to it. And this word does not require from one who believes in existence more than the belief in existence and oneness in an apparent and intuitive way without reflection. Then we heard of one who said it in the early days of Islam and did not know after it the obligations of wudu' and prayer, or whether He (Allah) is everlasting by an everlastingness or by Himself, and similar items of knowledge. And nothing repels the obviousness of this except an obstinate person or one ignorant of the biography of the Salaf and what occurred among them. And it indicates the strength of this aspect in the Shari'a that whoever is examined about this state and it is verified from him, and he refuses to submit to learning what is beyond what he has, no one misses [him?]...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and argument. Ghazali begins by stating that from knowledge and the apparent meanings of Shari'a, the first state (complete belief by taqlid) is on salvation and properly called iman and islam. Then he turns to the second state (those who believe only in existence, etc.). He notes that the early Salaf did not issue a clear ruling that such a person leaves iman/islam. Later scholars differ, with many fearing that such minimal belief without more might remove one from islam. But Ghazali argues that it is not unlikely that many converts from among the rough, commoners, women, and followers had exactly that minimal belief (just the shahada). He then asks: if they were asked about attributes like will, speech, etc., they would be ignorant of them. How then could such a person be removed from islam? He points to the Prophet's practice of accepting the shahada alone and sparing lives. The shahada only necessitates belief in existence and oneness in an intuitive way without deep reflection. He gives the example of early converts who said the shahada but did not know about wudu, prayer, or whether Allah has an attribute of everlastingness. He concludes that only an obstinate person or one ignorant of the Salaf's practice would deny this. Finally, he states that if such a person is examined and confirmed to have this state, and he refuses to learn more, 'no one missed' — likely meaning that no one from the Salaf considered him a disbeliever or that he is not lost from islam. The argument strongly supports the sufficiency of the shahada for basic islam.

Key Terms
شهادة
إيمان
إسلام
السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf required detailed theological knowledge for valid Islam.
Correction: Ghazali shows that the Salaf accepted the shahada alone, and did not require knowledge of attributes, wudu, prayer, etc., for basic Islam.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the basis for judging someone to be a Muslim?
A) Knowledge of all attributes of God.
B) Belief in existence and oneness via the shahada.
C) Performance of all religious duties.
D) Acceptance of detailed theological formulations.

Key Takeaway
The shahada alone is sufficient for basic Islam, as proven by the Prophet's practice and the Salaf's precedent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever looked down on someone for not knowing detailed theology? How does this passage challenge you to reconsider your judgment of others' faith?
?
The shahada alone was enough for the early companions. Do you treat the shahada as the foundation of your own Islam, or do you secretly rely on your knowledge and deeds to feel secure?
?
If you met a sincere person who only says 'La ilaha illa Allah' and knows nothing else, would you consider them Muslim? Are you willing to follow the Prophet's example and accept them without demanding more?

The Salvation of Simple Faith: The First State and the Shahada
Ghazali presents the ruling on the first and second states of faith and explains the sufficiency of the shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that simple faith in God and the Prophet, without detailed theological knowledge, is sufficient for salvation and that the early scholars did not excommunicate such believers.

Core Idea
Simple faith suffices for salvation—God's mercy is not limited by theological complexity.

Ghazali begins by establishing the principle that the first state of believers—those with minimal but sincere faith—are on the path of salvation. He then addresses the second state, explaining that the early Salaf did not remove such people from the fold of Islam, and that later scholars were cautious. This passage introduces the core argument that the shahada itself does not require more than a basic belief in God's existence and oneness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two states
Read the passage and locate where Ghazali describes the first and second states of believers. Notice the ruling he gives for each.
The first state is clearly defined as being on a path of salvation.
2
Understand the Salaf's stance
Pay attention to Ghazali's claim that the earlier Salaf did not remove holders of simple creed from Islam. Contrast with the later scholars' differing views.
This shows a difference between early and later practice.
3
Reflect on the early Muslim example
Consider the Bedouins, weak women, and followers who accepted Islam without detailed knowledge. Ghazali uses this to show that such faith was common and accepted.
This is a key evidence from the early community.
4
Analyze the meaning of the shahada
Ghazali states that the word 'La ilaha illallah' does not require more than a basic, intuitive belief in God's existence and oneness. Understand how this supports his argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يدل عليه العلم، ويستنبط من ظواهر الشرع، أن أرباب الحالة الأولى على سبيل نجاة، ووصف إيمان وإسلام. وأما أهل الحالة الثانية: فالمتقدمون من السلف لم يشتهر عنهم في صورة هذه المسألة يخرج صاحب العقيدة عن حكم الإيمان والإسلام. والمتأخرون مختلفون، وكثير خاف أن يخرج من اعتقاد وإظهار الإقرار به ونبيه من الإسلام. ولا يبعد أن يكون كثير ممن أسلم من الأجلاف والرعيات وضعفاء النساء والأتباع هذا عقده بلا مزيد عليه. ولو سئلوا واستكشفوا عن الله عز وجل هل له إرادة أو كلام أو بقاء أو ما شاكل ذلك؟ وهل له صفات معنوية ليست هي هو ولا هي غيره؟ ربما وجدوا ويجهلون ذلك ولا يعقلون وجه ما يخاطبون به. وكيف يخرج من حكم الإسلام من اعتقد وجود الله ووحدانيته مع الإقرار بالنبوة؟ والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قد رفع القتال والقتل عنهم، فأوجب حكم الإيمان والإسلام لمن قال لا إله إلا الله وعقد عليها. وهذه الكلمة لا تقتضي أكثر من اعتقاد الوجود والوحدة في الظاهر وعلى البديهة من غير نظر. ثم سمعنا عمن قالها في صدر الإسلام ولم يعلم بعدها الفرائض الوضوء والصلاة، أو هو باق ببقاء أو بنفسه وأشباه هذه المعارف. ولا يدفع ظهور هذا إلا معاند أو جاهل بسيرة السلف وما جرى بينهم. ويدل على قوة هذا الجانب في الشرع أن من استكشف منه على هذه الحالة وتحققت منه وأبى أن يذعن إلى تعلم ما زاد على ما عنده، لم يفت أحد بقتله ولا باسترقاقه، والحكم عليه بالخلود في النار عسير جدا وخطر عظيم، مع ثبوت الشرع بأن من قال لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة.
And that which knowledge indicates, and is derived from the outward meanings of the Law, is that the people of the first state are on a path of salvation, and are described with faith and Islam. As for the people of the second state: the earlier ones among the Salaf are not known to have, in the form of this issue, removed the holder of a creed from the ruling of faith and Islam. And the later ones differed, and many feared that one who believed and showed acceptance of Him and His Prophet would be removed from Islam. And it is not unlikely that many of those who embraced Islam from the Bedouins, the herdsmen, the weak women, and the followers have this as their creed without addition. And if they were asked and investigated about Allah Almighty: does He have will, speech, abidingness, or the like? And does He have attribute meanings that are not He nor other than He? Perhaps they would find that they are ignorant of that and do not understand the meaning of what is addressed to them. And how can one who believes in the existence of God and His Oneness along with acceptance of prophethood be removed from the ruling of Islam? And the Prophet (peace be upon him) lifted fighting and killing from them, so he made the ruling of faith and Islam obligatory for whoever says 'There is no god but Allah' and holds firmly to it. And this word does not require more than the belief in existence and oneness in the outward and intuitively without reflection. Then we have heard of those who said it in early Islam and did not know after it the obligations of ablution and prayer, or whether He is abiding by an abidingness or by Himself, and similar cognitions. And nothing repels the manifestness of this except an obstinate person or one ignorant of the conduct of the Salaf and what occurred among them. And it indicates the strength of this aspect in the Law that one who is examined about this state and it is verified from him and he refuses to submit to learning more than what he has, no one gave a legal verdict to kill him or enslave him, and judging him to be eternally in the Fire is very difficult and a great danger, with the Law established that whoever says 'There is no god but Allah' enters Paradise.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a legal-theological argument by Imam Ghazali defending the view that simple faith in God and the Prophet is sufficient for salvation, and that ignorance of detailed divine attributes does not remove one from Islam. He begins by stating that the people of the first state (those with minimal but sincere belief) are on the path of salvation and are described as believers and Muslims. As for the people of the second state (those who may have some doubts or lack detailed knowledge), he notes that the earlier Salaf did not explicitly rule on removing such people from the category of faith and Islam. Later scholars differed, but many feared excommunicating those who simply believed in God and His Prophet without further elaboration. Ghazali supports this by pointing to the many early converts from among the Bedouins, weak women, and followers who had a simple creed without additional details. He poses a rhetorical question: if such people were asked about God's attributes like will, speech, or abidingness, or about attributes that are neither identical to God nor other than Him, they would be ignorant and not understand the terminology. Nevertheless, they should not be removed from Islam because they believe in God's existence and oneness and accept the Prophet. He cites the prophetic practice that the Prophet did not fight or kill people merely for lack of detailed knowledge; rather, he accepted the mere utterance of 'La ilaha illallah' and considered it sufficient for the ruling of faith and Islam. This phrase requires only the belief in God's existence and oneness in an intuitive, not reflective, manner. Ghazali then gives historical examples of early Muslims who said the shahada but were unaware of the obligations of prayer or the nature of God's attributes. He asserts that only an obstinate person or one ignorant of the Salaf would deny this manifest evidence. He strengthens his argument by noting that no jurist gave a verdict to kill or enslave a person who, upon examination, refused to learn more than his simple belief. To judge such a person as eternally in Hellfire is extremely difficult and dangerous, given the established hadith that whoever says 'La ilaha illallah' enters Paradise.

Key Terms
الحالة الأولى
الحالة الثانية
السلف
الخلف
لا إله إلا الله
كلمة التوحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a person must have detailed knowledge of God's attributes and theological nuances to be considered a Muslim and saved.
Correction: Ghazali argues that the mere utterance of the shahada with sincere belief in God's existence and oneness and acceptance of the Prophet is sufficient for the ruling of Islam and salvation, as shown by the practice of the Salaf and the Prophet.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the minimum requirement for a person to be considered within the ruling of Islam and faith?
A) Belief in God's existence and oneness along with acceptance of prophethood
B) Knowledge of all divine attributes
C) Full performance of all religious obligations
D) Rejection of any intellectual inquiry

Key Takeaway
Ghazali argues that the mere utterance of 'La ilaha illallah' with heartfelt belief is sufficient to be considered a Muslim and is on the path to salvation, regardless of lack of detailed theological knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever looked down on someone whose faith seemed 'simple' or 'uninformed'? How does Ghazali's argument about the people of the first state challenge your heart? Will you actively seek to remove pride from your heart today and ask Allah for sincere humility?
?
If you were stripped of all your theological knowledge and could only say 'La ilaha illallah' with conviction, would you be at peace with your salvation? This lesson says yes. Do you truly believe that? Read the Arabic phrase 'لا إله إلا الله' slowly. Does it fill you with the same certainty as when you first believed? If not, what is missing? Commit today to renew your shahada from your heart.
?
Ghazali points out that even early converts had a simple creed. Think of a specific person in your life right now who may not know much about Islam but believes in God and His Prophet. What is your attitude toward them? Will you change how you treat them after this lesson? Write down one concrete thing you will do to honor their faith rather than judge their lack of knowledge.

Prophetic Evidence and the Danger of Takfir
Ghazali provides historical examples and legal reasoning to support the sufficiency of simple faith and warns against declaring such people eternally damned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic evidence and legal consequences that support the sufficiency of simple faith, and the danger of declaring such believers to be eternally in Hell.

Core Idea
Prophetic practice and legal rulings confirm that simple faith guarantees Paradise.

Ghazali continues his argument by citing historical examples of early Muslims who had simple faith yet were not obligated to learn further. He then strengthens his case with the legal principle that no jurist ruled to kill or enslave such a person, and warns against the grave danger of condemning them to eternal Hell. This lesson solidifies the evidence from practice and law.

Guided Path
1
Examine the historical examples
Read about the early Muslims who only knew the shahada and were unaware of obligations like prayer or details about God's attributes.
These examples from early Islam show that simple faith was accepted.
2
Recognize the legal consequence
Notice that no jurist gave a verdict to kill or enslave a person who refused to learn more than simple faith.
This indicates the legal protection given to such believers.
3
Understand the danger of eternal damnation
Ghazali warns that judging such a person to be in Hell forever is very difficult and dangerous, contradicting the hadith that whoever says 'La ilaha illallah' enters Paradise.
This is a strong argument against takfir of simple believers.

Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a legal-theological argument by Imam Ghazali defending the view that simple faith in God and the Prophet is sufficient for salvation, and that ignorance of detailed divine attributes does not remove one from Islam. He begins by stating that the people of the first state (those with minimal but sincere belief) are on the path of salvation and are described as believers and Muslims. As for the people of the second state (those who may have some doubts or lack detailed knowledge), he notes that the earlier Salaf did not explicitly rule on removing such people from the category of faith and Islam. Later scholars differed, but many feared excommunicating those who simply believed in God and His Prophet without further elaboration. Ghazali supports this by pointing to the many early converts from among the Bedouins, weak women, and followers who had a simple creed without additional details. He poses a rhetorical question: if such people were asked about God's attributes like will, speech, or abidingness, or about attributes that are neither identical to God nor other than Him, they would be ignorant and not understand the terminology. Nevertheless, they should not be removed from Islam because they believe in God's existence and oneness and accept the Prophet. He cites the prophetic practice that the Prophet did not fight or kill people merely for lack of detailed knowledge; rather, he accepted the mere utterance of 'La ilaha illallah' and considered it sufficient for the ruling of faith and Islam. This phrase requires only the belief in God's existence and oneness in an intuitive, not reflective, manner. Ghazali then gives historical examples of early Muslims who said the shahada but were unaware of the obligations of prayer or the nature of God's attributes. He asserts that only an obstinate person or one ignorant of the Salaf would deny this manifest evidence. He strengthens his argument by noting that no jurist gave a verdict to kill or enslave a person who, upon examination, refused to learn more than his simple belief. To judge such a person as eternally in Hellfire is extremely difficult and dangerous, given the established hadith that whoever says 'La ilaha illallah' enters Paradise.

Key Terms
السلف
لا إله إلا الله
النار
الجنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a person who refuses to learn more about Islam beyond the shahada should be killed or is doomed to Hell.
Correction: Ghazali shows that no jurist gave such a ruling, and that the hadith promises Paradise for those who sincerely say 'La ilaha illallah'.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what did no jurist rule for a person who, after examination, refused to learn more than his simple faith?
A) Kill him or enslave him
B) Imprison him
C) Excommunicate him
D) Force him to learn

Key Takeaway
Ghazali concludes that the Law itself protects those with simple faith, and that declaring them eternally damned contradicts the prophetic promise that 'whoever says La ilaha illallah enters Paradise.'

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever looked down on a fellow Muslim who seemed ignorant of Islamic rulings or theology? After reading this passage, how must you change your attitude toward such a person?
?
If you were put in a position to defend someone who only knows the shahada and refuses to learn more, would you be able to stand by Ghazali's argument and trust the Prophet's promise? What holds you back?
?
This passage warns that declaring someone eternally damned is a 'great danger.' Do you have any prejudice in your heart that leads you to think someone might be beyond Allah's mercy? How does this prophetic evidence challenge that assumption?
