Faith as Inner Affirmation (Tasdiq)
Ghazali presents the case and argues that iman is pure tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ghazali's argument that the essence of faith (iman) is inner affirmation of the heart (tasdiq), not verbal utterance.

Core Idea
Faith lives in the heart; the tongue only translates it.

Ghazali addresses a pressing question: can a person be a believer without uttering the shahada? He argues that since iman is fundamentally inner conviction, silence does not negate it. This lesson unpacks his core argument and the supporting hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation. Notice how Ghazali first presents the case of the silent believer and then gives his ruling.
2
Identify the definition
Find where Ghazali defines iman as 'al-tasdiq al-mahd'. Understand that this is his foundational claim.
3
Connect to the hadith
The Prophet's hadith about the mustard seed is used to show that even minimal inner faith secures salvation. Reflect on why this supports Ghazali's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بكلمتى الشهادة (۱) ، وعلم وجوبها ولكنه لم ينطق بها ، فيحتمل أن يجعل إمتناعه عن النطق كامتناعه عن الصلاة (۲) ونقول : هو مؤمن غير مخلد في النار ، والإيمان هو التصديق المحض (۳) ، واللسان ترجمان الإيمان فلا بد ان يكون الإيمان موجوداً بتمامه قبل اللسان حتى يترجمه اللسان ، وهذا هو الأظهر ، إذ لا مستند إلا إتباع موجب الألفاظ ووضع اللسان (٤) إن الإيمان هو عبارة عن التصديق بالقلب (٥) . وقد قال صلى الله عليه وسلم يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة (٦) ولا ينعدم الإيمان من القلب بالسكوت عن النطق الواجب (٧) ، كما لا ينعدم بالسكوت عن الفعل الواجب وقال قائلون : القول ركن (۸) إذ ليس كلمتا الشهادة اخباراً عن القلب بل هو إنشاء عقد آخر وابتداء شهادة وإلتزام ، والأول أظهر (۹) ، وقد غلا في هذا طائفة المرجئة فقالوا : هذا لا يدخل النار أصلا(۱) وقالوا : إن المؤمن وإن عصى فلا يدخل النار ، وسنبطل ذلك عليهم
الهامش:
(۱) هما لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم.
(۲) بعد حلول وقتها وعلمه بوجوبها
(۳) الخالص بما جاء به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم
(٤) العربي، أي الذي يوجبه أصل الوضع العربي
(٥) لأن محل التصديق القلب ولم يقيده أهل اللسان إلا أنه معلوم لهم ذلك
(٦) تقدم الكلام عليه
(۷) بعد علمه بوجوبه كما لا ينعدم بالسكوت عن الفعل الواجب وهو العمل ، وبين السكوت ، جناس .
(۸) أي النطق باللسان بالشهادتين ركن من أركان الإيمان
(۹) أي كونه إخباراً عن القلب باعتبار أن اللسان ترجمانه ، وممن ذهب إلى هذا القول الكراميه ومن وافقهم جعلوا القول ركنا في مفهوم الإيمان فلا يثبت الإيمان إلا به .
(۱) (من ص250) غلا فيمن صدق بالقلب وامتنع عن النطق مع علمه بوجوبه ومساعدة الوقت طائفة المرجئة وهي من طوائف المبتدعة الذين من فضائحهم قولهم إنه لا يضر مع الإيمان معصية كما لا ينفع مع الكفر طاعة ، لما تقدم من زعمهم أن المعصية لا تضر مع الإيمان وهنا قد وجد الإيمان غير أنه عصى بإمتناعه عن النطق .
With the two words of the testimony (shahada) (1), and he knows their obligation but does not utter them, it is possible to make his abstention from utterance like his abstention from prayer (2). And we say: He is a believer, not eternally in the Fire. And faith (iman) is pure affirmation (tasdiq) (3), and the tongue is the translator of faith, so faith must exist in its entirety before the tongue so that the tongue may translate it. And this is the more apparent, for there is no basis except following the implication of the words and the usage of the (Arabic) tongue (4) that faith is an expression of affirmation by the heart (5). And he (peace be upon him) said: 'There will come out of the Fire whoever has in his heart a mustard seed's weight (of faith)' (6). And faith does not cease from the heart by silence about the obligatory utterance (7), just as it does not cease by silence about the obligatory act. And some said: Utterance (qawl) is a pillar (rukn) (8), for the two words of testimony are not news about the heart, but rather the establishment of another contract and the initiation of testimony and commitment. And the first (view) is more apparent (9). And a group of the Murji'ah went to extremes in this, saying: This person will never enter the Fire at all (1), and they said: The believer, even if he disobeys, will not enter the Fire. And we will refute that against them.
Margins:
(1) They are: 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' (peace be upon him).
(2) After its time arrives and his knowledge of its obligation.
(3) The pure (affirmation) with what the Prophet (peace be upon him) brought.
(4) The Arabic (tongue), i.e., that which the origin of Arabic usage requires.
(5) Because the place of affirmation is the heart, and the people of the tongue did not restrict it, but that is known to them.
(6) The discussion on it has preceded.
(7) After his knowledge of its obligation, just as it does not cease by silence about the obligatory act, which is action. And between 'silence' (al-sukut) and (the previous) there is paronomasia (jinas).
(8) i.e., utterance by the tongue of the two testimonies is a pillar of the pillars of faith.
(9) i.e., it being news about the heart by virtue of the tongue being its translator. Among those who adopted this view are the Karamiyyah and those who agreed with them; they made utterance a pillar in the concept of faith, so faith is only established through it.
(1) (from p.250) The Murji'ah sect—among the innovating sects whose scandals include their saying that no sin harms with faith just as no obedience benefits with disbelief—went to extremes regarding one who affirms with the heart but refrains from utterance despite knowing its obligation and having the opportunity, because they claim that sin does not harm with faith, and here faith exists but he sinned by refraining from utterance.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the nature of faith (iman). The author, Imam al-Ghazali, addresses the case of a person who knows the two testimonies (shahada) and knows they are obligatory, yet does not utter them. He first states that one might analogize this to omitting a required prayer, but then he gives the correct position: such a person is a believer and will not be eternally punished in the Fire. He grounds this on the definition of iman as pure inner affirmation (tasdiq) of the heart. The tongue is merely the translator of that inner faith; the faith must exist fully in the heart before the tongue can express it. Ghazali asserts this is the more apparent view, because linguistic usage points to 'iman' meaning heart-affirmation. He supports this with the hadith that those with even a mustard seed of faith will leave the Fire. He argues that silence about the obligatory utterance does not negate faith from the heart, just as silence about an obligatory action does not negate it (though sin occurs). Then he presents a counterargument: some say utterance is a pillar (rukn) because the shahada is not merely reporting inner belief but initiating a new contract. Ghazali dismisses this as less apparent. Finally, he mentions the extreme Murji'ah who claim such a person will never enter the Fire at all, and that sin does not harm faith—a view he promises to refute. This passage clearly establishes Ghazali's position that iman is essentially tasdiq, and that verbal utterance is not constitutive of faith, though obligatory.

Key Terms
إيمان
تصديق
نطق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that iman requires verbal utterance as a pillar; Ghazali shows it is only the translator of inner affirmation.
Correction: Ghazali emphasizes that iman is essentially tasdiq of the heart; utterance is a separate obligation but not constitutive of faith.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the essence of iman?
A) Utterance with the tongue
B) Affirmation by the heart
C) Both affirmation and utterance
D) Actions of the limbs

Key Takeaway
Iman is inner truth; the tongue only reveals what the heart already holds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith is purely inner affirmation, is your outward practice merely a translation of what is already inside, or are you using actions to fake what is missing in your heart?
?
The hadith promises that even a mustard seed of tasdiq will save you. Do you have that mustard seed, or have you been relying on your tongue and deeds to compensate for an empty heart?
?
Ghazali says the tongue is only a translator. If your tongue were silent forever, would your heart still be a believer? What does your answer reveal about where you truly place your security?

Utterance as Pillar? The Murji'ah Extreme
Ghazali responds to the view that utterance is a pillar and critiques the Murji'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the counterargument that utterance is a pillar of faith and why Ghazali rejects it, as well as the extreme Murji'ah position.

Core Idea
Utterance is a translator, not a pillar; the Murji'ah overcorrect by denying all punishment.

After establishing that iman is inner affirmation, Ghazali addresses a counterview that makes verbal utterance a pillar of faith. He then exposes the extreme Murji'ah who claim that even a silent believer will never enter the Fire. This lesson explores those views and Ghazali's response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation. Note the two opposing views presented.
2
Understand the counterargument
The counterargument states that the shahada is not a report about inner faith but a new contract (insha'). Identify why this makes utterance a pillar.
3
Ghazali's response
He says the first view (utterance as translator) is more apparent. Consider why he finds it more convincing.
4
The Murji'ah extreme
The Murji'ah go beyond, claiming the silent believer will never enter the Fire. Recognize why Ghazali considers this an exaggeration.

The Hypocrite: Worldly vs. Afterlife Rulings
Ghazali distinguishes afterlife punishment from worldly Muslim treatment for one who utters without belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between outward and inward rulings for a person who utters the shahada without belief, and the areas of certainty and doubt in Islamic jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Outwardly Muslim, inwardly disbeliever: worldly rulings follow the tongue, afterlife follows the heart.

Imam al-Ghazali presents a nuanced case: a person who says the shahada but does not affirm inwardly. How should we treat such a person? The answer depends on the domain—this world or the next. Ghazali clarifies what is certain and what remains open to scholarly consideration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two certain rulings
Read the passage and locate where Ghazali says 'we have no doubt' about the afterlife and worldly rulings.
Notice the contrast between hukm al-akhira and hukm al-dunya.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is the hypocrite a disbeliever in the afterlife? Because he lacks tasdiq (affirmation) in his heart. Why is he treated as Muslim in this world? Because rulers judge by outward appearance.
The heart is hidden; we assume consistency between tongue and heart.
3
Examine the doubtful matter
Ghazali introduces a third scenario: internal rulings between the person and Allah, such as inheritance and marriage. Note that he does not give a definitive answer.
This shows the limits of human knowledge and the role of ijtihad.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters: it protects the integrity of worldly dealings while upholding the seriousness of faith in the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدرجة السادسة : أن يقول بلسانه : لا اله الا الله محمد رسول الله ولكن لم يصدق بقلبه (۲) ، فلا نشك في أن هذا في حكم الآخرة من الكفار ، وإنه مخلد في النار (٣) . ولا نشك في انه في حكم الدنيا الذي يتعلق بالائمة والولاة، من المسلمين (٤) ، لأن قلبه لا يطلع عليه (٥) وعلينا أن نظن به أنه ما قاله(٦) بلسانه إلا وهو منطو عليه في قلبه ، وإنما نشك في أمر ثالث وهو الحكم الدنيوي فيما بينه الله تعالى ، وذلك بأن يموت له في الحال مسلم ثم يصدق بعد ذلك بقلبه ثم يستفتي ويقول : وبين كنت غير مصدق بالقلب حالة الموت (۷) والميراث الآن في يدي فهل يحل لي بيني وبين الله تعالى ؟ أو نكح مسلمة ثم صدق بقلبه هل تلزمه إعادة النكاح ؟، هذا فيحتمل ان يقال محل نظر
الهامش:
(۲) أي لم يستقر ذلك التصديق بقلبه
(٣) لأنه قد عدم المسمى الإيمان الذي هو التصديق .
(٤) لأنه ليس لهم إلا الظواهر والتصديق محله القلب
(٥) لأنه أمر غيب عنا وما كلفنا بإطلاعه ، وإنما الحكم عليه بالإمارات.
(٦) يعني القول المذكور من اداء الشهادتين
(۷) أي موت ذلك القريب الذي ورثته وإنما كنت مسلما باللسان فقط .
The sixth degree: that he says with his tongue: 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' but he does not affirm (tasdiq) with his heart (2). Then we have no doubt that this person, in the judgment of the afterlife (al-akhira), is among the disbelievers, and he is eternally in the Fire (3). And we have no doubt that in the worldly judgment (hukm al-dunya) pertaining to rulers and governors, he is among the Muslims (4), because his heart is not accessible to them (5). And it is required of us to assume that he only said it (6) with his tongue while it was inwardly contained in his heart. But we doubt concerning a third matter: the worldly judgment (hukm dunyawi) between him and Allah, the Exalted. That is, if a Muslim relative dies while he is in that state (i.e., only uttering), and then later he affirms with his heart, and then he seeks a fatwa and says: 'I was not affirming with my heart at the time of death (7), and the inheritance is now in my hand; is it permissible for me between me and Allah? Or if he married a Muslim woman and then affirmed with his heart, is he obliged to renew the marriage?' This is open to consideration (mahall nazar).
Margins:
(2) i.e., that affirmation did not settle in his heart.
(3) Because he lacks the reality of iman, which is affirmation.
(4) Because they have only external appearances, and affirmation's place is the heart.
(5) Because it is a matter unseen by us, and we are not tasked with knowing it; judgment is based on indications.
(6) i.e., the aforementioned utterance of performing the two testimonies.
(7) i.e., the death of that relative whose inheritance he received, while he was only Muslim by tongue.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage defines and discusses the sixth degree of people regarding the shahada: one who utters the two testimonies with his tongue but does not genuinely affirm with his heart (i.e., a hypocrite/munafiq). Ghazali states two certainties: (1) In the afterlife (al-akhira), such a person is a disbeliever eternally in the Fire, because he lacks the reality of iman (affirmation). (2) In worldly rulings (hukm al-dunya) pertaining to human authorities, he is treated as a Muslim in matters like inheritance, marriage, etc., because we judge by outward appearances; his inner state is hidden from us, and we are required to assume he is truthful. Then Ghazali introduces a third, doubtful matter: the inner ruling between the person and Allah (i.e., in conscience and religious obligation). He presents two scenarios: (a) If a relative dies while the person is outwardly Muslim but inwardly disbelieving, and later he truly believes and receives the inheritance, is it permissible for him (between him and Allah) to keep it? (b) If he married a Muslim woman while a hypocrite and then later believed, is he required to renew the marriage? Ghazali leaves these questions as 'open to consideration' (mahall nazar), indicating scholarly disagreement or need for further investigation. The footnotes clarify that the person lacked settled affirmation, and that worldly rulers rely only on outward signs.

درجة سادسة
نفاق
حكم الآخرة
حكم الدنيا
ظاهر
باطن
محل نظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person who says the shahada is always a believer in this world and the next.
Correction: Ghazali explains that while worldly rulings treat such a person as Muslim due to outward appearance, the afterlife depends on inner belief, and certain internal matters remain open to scholarly consideration.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, how is a person who utters the shahada but does not affirm with his heart treated in worldly rulings?
A) As a disbeliever
B) As a Muslim
C) As a sinner requiring re-conversion
D) As a believer with incomplete faith

Key Takeaway
The hypocrite is treated as Muslim in this world due to outward appearance, but in the afterlife he is among the disbelievers; certain internal matters remain subject to scholarly consideration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If your inner disbelief were exposed to everyone, would you still be treated as Muslim? Does that thought unsettle you enough to examine your own heart today?
?
Ghazali leaves certain matters 'open to consideration' for the hypocrite who later believes. How much weight do you place on your outward acts of worship without checking the state of your heart? What is one practical step you will take this week to align your tongue and heart?

The Sixth Degree: Hypocrisy and Its Two Certain Rulings
Ghazali defines the sixth degree (hypocrisy) and states its two certain rulings in the Hereafter and worldly matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of hypocrisy (nifaq) according to Ghazali and the two certain rulings that apply to the hypocrite: eternal punishment in the Hereafter and treatment as a Muslim in worldly affairs.

Core Idea
The hypocrite is a disbeliever in the Hereafter but a Muslim in the eyes of worldly rulers.

In this passage, Ghazali introduces the sixth degree of faith: hypocrisy. He distinguishes between the hypocrite's inner disbelief and outer profession of Islam, clarifying the absolute rulings in the Hereafter and the relative rulings in this world. This foundation is crucial for understanding how Islamic law deals with hidden disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms: الدرجة السادسة, النفاق, التصديق, أحكام الدنيا, أحكام الآخرة.
2
Identify the definition of the sixth degree
Find the sentence that defines the sixth degree. It specifies saying the shahada with the tongue but not believing with the heart.
This is the core definition of hypocrisy in this context.
3
Understand the two certain rulings
Ghazali says 'we do not doubt' in two rulings: one in the Hereafter (kafir, eternal Fire) and one in worldly dealings (considered Muslim). Ask yourself: why is there no doubt? Because his heart is not known to us, and we must judge by the apparent.
These two rulings are the foundation for the next lessons.

هذا لا يدخل النار أصلا. وقالوا : إن المؤمن وإن عصى فلا يدخل النار ، وسنبطل ذلك عليهم. الدرجة السادسة : أن يقول بلسانه : لا اله الا الله محمد رسول الله ولكن لم يصدق بقلبه (۲) ، فلا نشك في أن هذا في حكم الآخرة من الكفار ، وإنه مخلد في النار (٣) . ولا نشك في انه في حكم الدنيا الذي يتعلق بالائمة والولاة، من المسلمين (٤) ، لأن قلبه لا يطلع عليه (٥) وعلينا أن نظن به أنه ما قاله(٦) بلسانه إلا وهو منطو عليه في قلبه ، وإنما نشك في أمر ثالث وهو الحكم الدنيوي فيما بينه الله تعالى ، وذلك بأن يموت له في الحال مسلم ثم يصدق بعد ذلك بقلبه ثم يستفتي ويقول : كنت غير مصدق بالقلب حالة الموت (۷) والميراث الآن في يدي فهل يحل لي بيني وبين الله تعالى ؟ أو نكح مسلمة ثم صدق بقلبه هل تلزمه إعادة النكاح ؟، هذا فيحتمل ان يقال محل نظر. أحكام الدنيا منوطة بالقول الظاهر (۱) ظاهراً وباطناً(٢) ، ويحتمل أن يقال : تناط بالظاهر في حق غيره ، لأن باطنه غير ظاهر لغيره ، وباطنه ظاهر له في نفسه بينه وبين الله تعالى. والأظهر والعلم عند الله تعالى (۳) ، إنه لا يحل له ذلك الميراث (٤)، ويلزمه إعادة النكاح . ولذلك كان حذيفة (٥) رضي الله عنه لا يحضر جنازة من يموت من المنافقين ، وعمر رضي الله عنه كان يراعي ذلك منه فلا يحضر إذا لم يحضر حذيفة الله عنه ، والصلاة فعل ظاهر في الدنيا وإن كان من العبادات . والتوقي. الحرام أيضاً من جملة ما يجب الله ، كالصلاة (٦) ، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «طلب الحلال فريضة بعد الفريضة» (۷)، وليس هذا مناقضاً لقولنا إن الإرث
This one does not enter the Fire at all. And they said: The believer, even if he disobeys, will not enter the Fire, and we will refute that against them. The sixth degree: that he says with his tongue 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' but did not believe with his heart (2), so we do not doubt that this one, in the ruling of the Hereafter, is of the disbelievers, and that he is eternally [punished] in the Fire (3). And we do not doubt that he, in the worldly ruling that pertains to the imams and rulers, is of the Muslims (4), because his heart is not known (5), and it is upon us to think of him that he only said it (6) with his tongue while it was [also] concealed in his heart. But we doubt in a third matter: the worldly ruling between him and Allah the Exalted, such as if a Muslim relative of his dies [while he is still a hypocrite] and then he believes after that with his heart, then he seeks a fatwa and says: 'I was not believing in my heart at the time of death (7), and the inheritance is now in my hand, so is it permissible for me before Allah the Exalted [to keep it]? Or if he married a Muslim woman and then believed with his heart, is he required to renew the marriage?' This can be considered an issue. The worldly rulings are tied to the outward statement (1) outwardly and inwardly (2), and it is possible to say: they are tied to the outward [in dealings] with others, because his inward is not apparent to others, while his inward is apparent to himself between him and Allah the Exalted. And the more apparent—and knowledge is with Allah the Exalted (3)—is that the inheritance is not permissible for him (4), and he is required to renew the marriage. That is why Hudhayfa (5), may Allah be pleased with him, did not attend the funeral of one who died among the hypocrites, and Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, heeded him in that and did not attend if Hudhayfa did not attend, may Allah be pleased with him. And prayer is an outward action in the world even though it is an act of worship. And avoiding the unlawful is also among what Allah has obligated, like prayer (6), due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Seeking lawful [provision] is an obligation after [other] obligations' (7). And this does not contradict our statement that inheritance [is tied to outward Islam].
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage defines the sixth degree of those who profess faith but are not true believers — the hypocrite. It is a classification passage, specifying that the hypocrite only says the shahada with his tongue without heart-felt belief. Ghazali then states two certainties: first, in the Hereafter, such a person is among the disbelievers and will be eternally in the Fire; second, in worldly rulings handled by authorities (imams and governors), he is treated as a Muslim because his inner state is unknown to them. We must assume that his outward statement reflects his inner belief until proven otherwise. However, Ghazali introduces a third, doubtful case: if a person was a hypocrite at the time of a Muslim relative's death and then later genuinely believes, what is the ruling regarding the inheritance he already received, or if he married a Muslim woman while a hypocrite and then believes, must he renew the marriage? Ghazali presents two possible opinions: one ties worldly rulings solely to the outward statement (applying both externally and before God), while the other ties them to the outward only in dealings with others, but the individual's own knowledge before God matters. The more apparent view (al-azhar) is that he is not entitled to the inheritance and must renew the marriage. Ghazali supports this with the practice of the companions Hudhayfa and Umar, who considered a person's outward Islam insufficient for funeral prayers if there were signs of hypocrisy. He then notes that prayer and avoiding the unlawful are obligations like seeking lawful provision, citing a hadith. This does not contradict the principle that worldly inheritances are tied to outward Islam, because the hypocrite's outward Islam is valid for worldly rulings but does not entitle him to benefits that depend on actual faith.

Key Terms
الدرجة السادسة
النفاق
التصديق
أحكام الدنيا
أحكام الآخرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Outward profession of faith alone makes one a believer in all respects.
Correction: Ghazali clarifies that while outward profession makes one a Muslim in worldly rulings, it does not guarantee salvation in the Hereafter; inner belief is required.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the ruling on a person who says the shahada with his tongue but does not believe in his heart?
A) He is a believer in both realms.
B) He is a disbeliever in both realms.
C) He is a disbeliever in the Hereafter and a Muslim in worldly rulings.
D) He is a Muslim in the Hereafter and a disbeliever in worldly rulings.

Key Takeaway
The hypocrite's outward Islam is valid for worldly dealings, but his inner disbelief condemns him to eternal punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever said the shahada or performed an Islamic act when your heart was elsewhere, feeling empty or doubtful? What does this lesson teach you about the weight of that inner state in Allah's sight? Will you seek to align your outward practice with inward sincerity starting today?
?
If your heart's true belief were to be tested, would the words you speak still carry weight? The hypocrite's eternal fate is the Fire—not because of missing actions, but because of a missing heart. Are you willing to examine tonight whether your Islam is merely lip-service or rooted in inner conviction?
?
This passage teaches that we cannot judge others' hearts—only Allah knows. But it also warns that we ourselves are judged by Allah based on what is in our hearts. If Allah were to expose your inner reality to others today, would you still be counted among the Muslims? What will you change to ensure your inner belief matches your outward actions?

The Doubtful Case: Worldly Rulings Between the Hypocrite and Allah
Ghazali discusses the third doubtful ruling for hypocrites regarding inheritance and marriage, presents two opinions, and supports the preferred view with companion practice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third, doubtful case regarding the hypocrite's worldly rulings between himself and Allah, and the preferred opinion on inheritance and marriage renewal, supported by the practice of the companions.

Core Idea
What is permissible for the hypocrite before Allah depends not only on outward statement but on inner belief.

After establishing the two clear rulings, Ghazali introduces a more nuanced case: a person who was a hypocrite at the time of inheriting or marrying, then later genuinely believes. This raises the question of whether the worldly acts were valid before Allah. The passage explores two possible views and presents the more apparent opinion, citing the companions Hudhayfa and Umar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage for Lesson 2, then the English translation. Note the specific examples of inheritance and marriage.
2
Identify the third doubtful matter
Ghazali says 'we doubt in a third matter'. Find what that is: rulings between the hypocrite and Allah when a relative dies or he marries while a hypocrite, then later believes.
This is different from the two certainties.
3
Understand the two opinions
One opinion ties rulings to outward statement only, both outwardly and before Allah. The other ties it to outward only in dealings with others, but the person's own knowledge matters. Which one does Ghazali prefer?
The preferred view is that the inheritance is not permissible and marriage must be renewed.
4
Learn the evidence from the companions
Ghazali cites Hudhayfa and Umar's practice of not praying over known hypocrites. This shows that outward Islam is not absolute when inner state is known (by divine insight).
Also note the hadith about seeking lawful provision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself going through the motions of worship—praying, fasting, giving charity—while your heart was distant, perhaps even doubting or disbelieving? If you later returned to sincere faith, would you be willing to confront those past actions and make amends, even if it costs you something dear, like a reputation or a relationship?
?
The hypocrite in this lesson is confronted with the truth of his past actions once he believes. Is there a sin in your past that you have never fully addressed because you thought that your later good deeds or repentance automatically erased it? What would it look like for you to 'rectify' that before Allah, even if others do not know?
?
Consider the practice of Hudhayfa and Umar: they did not treat hypocrites as believers in their funerals. Who in your life do you treat outwardly as a believer even though you know (or suspect) their heart is not with Allah? What would change if you acted on that knowledge? Does your own fear of hypocrisy prevent you from loving truth at all costs?

Faith and Disbelief

Outward Profession Determines Worldly Rulings
Defines the principle that worldly rulings are based on outward profession and applies it to inheritance, marriage, and funeral attendance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that worldly Islamic rulings are based on a person’s outward profession of faith, while inner belief is known only to Allah and will be judged accordingly.

Core Idea
Outward profession governs worldly judgments; inner faith is between the servant and Allah.

Imam al-Ghazali teaches a fundamental principle: the judgments of this world—such as inheritance, marriage, and funeral attendance—are based on what a person says and does outwardly, not on what is hidden in their heart. This allows the Muslim community to function while leaving ultimate judgment to Allah. In this passage, he applies this rule to the case of a secret apostate and illustrates it with the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the foundational principle
Read the opening sentence carefully: 'The rulings of this world are tied to the outward statement.' This means worldly judgments depend on what is expressed verbally and externally.
Note that this applies to the community's judgment, not Allah's knowledge.
2
Examine the application to a secret apostate
See how the principle applies: a person who outwardly professes Islam but inwardly apostatizes is still treated as Muslim in worldly matters like inheritance and marriage.
The passage specifically denies inheritance and requires renewing the marriage if the inner apostasy is known.
3
Observe the example of the Companions
Reflect on the practice of Hudhayfa and Umar: they avoided attending funerals of known hypocrites, acting on the knowledge of their inner state without publicly exposing them.
This shows how inner knowledge can influence personal actions but not public rulings.
4
Distinguish worldly from otherworldly accountability
Understand that the outward ruling does not negate inner accountability before Allah. The passage concludes that if one's inner state contradicts his outward submission, he will be held accountable by Allah.
This balances the principle with ultimate divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الدنيا منوطة بالقول الظاهر (۱) ظاهراً وباطناً(٢) ، ويحتمل أن يقال : تناط بالظاهر في حق غيره ، لأن باطنه غير ظاهر لغيره، وباطنه ظاهر له في نفسه بينه وبين الله تعالى. والأظهر والعلم عند الله تعالى (۳) ، إنه لا يحل له ذلك الميراث (٤)، ويلزمه إعادة النكاح . ولذلك كان حذيفة (٥) رضي الله عنه لا يحضر جنازة من يموت من المنافقين ، وعمر رضي الله عنه كان يراعي ذلك منه فلا يحضر إذا لم يحضر حذيفة الله عنه ، والصلاة فعل ظاهر في الدنيا وإن كان من العبادات . والتوقي. الحرام أيضاً من جملة ما يجب الله ، كالصلاة (٦) ، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : رضي عن طلب الحلال فريضة بعد الفريضة» (۷)، وليس هذا مناقضاً لقولنا إن الإرث (۱) الذي هو النطق بالشهادتين ، وعليه يترتب الحكم (۲) فعلى هذاله أخذ الميراث ، وإبقاء المسلمة على النكاح الأول بالنظر إلى الدنيا، وبالنظر إلى الآخر. (۳) أتى بهذه الجملة تبركا وتبريا من علمه إلى علم الله تعالى ، أي علمه محيط بكل شيء وهذا نظير ما يقول المفتي في آخر جوابه والله أعلم ، فيكل علمه إلى علم الله تعالى، ويتبرأ من أن يقول في دين الله ما ليس مطابقاً لما هو في نفس الأمر. (٤) لأنه لم يأخذه بحق القرابة في الحقيقة ، ولا توارث مع إختلاف الملل . (ه) حذيفة بن اليمان العبسي حليف بني عبد الأشهل، رضي الله عنه ، من خيار الصحابة ، وزهادهم ولاه عمر المدائن ، وله فتوحات ، مات سنة ست وثلاثين بعد مقتل عثمان بأربعين يوماً . (٦) أي حكمه كحكمها ، فإن قيل الإسلام هو الإنقياد الظاهر كما سبق ، والرجل المذكور قد ثبت له ذلك ، فيجوز الميراث نظرا إلى الظاهر وليس هو من أحكام الإيمان فيكون مناقضاً لقول الفقهاء الإرث حكم الإسلام والجواب ما أشار إليه المصنف بقوله : وليس هذا مناقضاً .. الخ (۷) أخرجه البيهقي عن ابن مسعود وضعفه ، وأخرجه الطبراني عن أنس بلفظ : طلب الحلال واجب على كل مسلم » . حكم الإسلام وهو الإستسلام، بل الاستسلام التام هو ما يشمل الظاهر والباطن(۱) فهذه الملاحظة إذا خالف الباطن الظاهر وعمل بهذه المخالفة تشبئاً بالظاهر يكون مؤاخذاً عند الله تعالى .
The rulings of this world are tied to the outward statement (1) outwardly and inwardly (2). And it is possible to say: they are tied to the outward with respect to others, because his inward is not apparent to others, and his inward is apparent to him in himself between him and Allah Almighty. And the more apparent—and knowledge is with Allah Almighty (3)—is that that inheritance is not permissible for him (4), and he must renew the marriage. For that reason, Hudhayfa (5), may Allah be pleased with him, used not to attend the funeral of a hypocrite who died, and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, observed that from him, so he would not attend if Hudhayfa did not attend. And prayer is an outward act in this world even if it is among acts of worship. And refraining from the unlawful is also among what is obligatory, like prayer (6), due to his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Seeking the lawful is an obligatory duty after the obligatory duty' (7). And this is not contradictory to our statement that inheritance (1) is the utterance of the two shahadahs, and upon it the ruling depends (2). So based on this, he takes the inheritance and the Muslim woman remains upon the first marriage with respect to this world, and with respect to the Hereafter. (3) He brought this sentence as a blessing and as a disavowal of his knowledge to the knowledge of Allah Almighty, meaning His knowledge encompasses everything, and this is similar to what the mufti says at the end of his answer: 'and Allah knows best'; he entrusts his knowledge to the knowledge of Allah Almighty and disavows that he says about the religion of Allah what is not in accordance with what is in reality. (4) Because he did not take it by right of kinship in reality, and there is no inheritance with difference of religions. (5) Hudhayfa ibn al-Yaman al-'Absi, ally of Banu 'Abd al-Ashhal, may Allah be pleased with him, among the best of the Companions and their ascetics; 'Umar put him in charge of al-Mada'in; he had conquests; he died in the year thirty-six, forty days after the murder of 'Uthman. (6) That is, its ruling is like its ruling (i.e., like prayer). For if it is said: Islam is outward submission as previously mentioned, and the mentioned man has established that, so inheritance is permissible with a view to the outward, and it is not among the rulings of faith, so it would contradict the statement of the jurists that inheritance is a ruling of Islam. The answer is what the author indicated by his saying: 'And this is not contradictory...' etc. (7) Al-Bayhaqi narrated it from Ibn Mas'ud and deemed it weak, and al-Tabarani narrated it from Anas with the wording: 'Seeking the lawful is obligatory upon every Muslim.' The ruling of Islam is submission (istislam); rather, complete submission is what includes the outward and the inward. (1) So this observation: if the inward contradicts the outward and he acts upon that contradiction pretending to be outwardly, he will be held accountable before Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a definition and application of the principle that worldly legal rulings (inheritance, marriage, funeral attendance) are based on outward profession of Islam, not on inner belief, which is known only to Allah. It begins by stating that worldly judgments are tied to the outward statement (al-qawl al-zahir), both outwardly and inwardly [in the sense that the inward confirms it]. It then clarifies that this ruling applies to others' judgment of a person, as his inner state is hidden. The settled opinion is that a secret apostate (who outwardly professes Islam but inwardly rejects) does not inherit, and his marriage must be renewed, but outwardly he is treated as a Muslim. This is exemplified by the practice of Hudhayfa, who knew the hypocrites and avoided their funerals, and 'Umar followed his lead. The passage then relates seeking lawful sustenance to obligatory acts like prayer, citing a hadith, and explains that this does not contradict the statement that inheritance is a ruling of Islam, because complete submission (istislam) encompasses both outward and inward. The footnotes expand on each point: the mufti's reliance on Allah's knowledge, the reason for denying inheritance (difference of religion), Hudhayfa's biography, the logical response to potential objections, and the authenticity of the hadith. The final footnote clarifies that if one contradicts his outward submission inwardly and acts on that contradiction while pretending to be outwardly compliant, he is held accountable by Allah.

Key Terms
القول الظاهر
الإستسلام
النفاق
الميراث
النكاح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think outward profession alone guarantees salvation in the afterlife.
Correction: This passage clarifies that outward profession only governs worldly rulings; inner faith is judged by Allah alone.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how are worldly rulings (e.g., inheritance, marriage) determined for a person who outwardly professes Islam but inwardly apostatizes?
A) Rulings are based on his inner belief, which is known to the Muslim community.
B) Rulings are based on his outward profession, so he is treated as a Muslim in worldly matters.
C) Rulings are suspended until his inner state becomes known through a miracle.
D) He is excommunicated immediately regardless of his outward statement.

Key Takeaway
Worldly rulings in Islam are based on outward submission, but ultimate accountability for inner faith rests with Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever relied on your outward acts of worship to feel secure, while ignoring the state of your heart? What would it take for you to stop hiding behind external obedience and confront your inner reality?
?
If Allah were to judge you today based only on what you truly believe in private, would you be safe? What is one hidden doubt or hypocrisy you need to repent from?
?
The author says that complete submission requires both outward and inward. In which area of your life is your outward compliance not matched by inner submission?

Ghazali's Refutation of Murji'ah Proofs
Ghazali refutes Murji'ah use of Quranic verses on iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ghazali argues that the Quranic verses the Murji'ah cite actually support the view that faith includes action, and how he defends this with hadith and Quran.

Core Idea
The Murji'ah misuse verses about faith; true faith is never without works.

Ghazali directly challenges the Murji'ah's proof-texts from the Quran. He cites seven verses they rely on, then turns their own evidence against them by explaining that the term 'iman' in those verses refers to Islam — conviction, speech, and action. This lesson follows his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses Murji'ah use
Read through the Arabic passage and identify the verses Ghazali quotes. Notice how each verse mentions 'iman' in a way that the Murji'ah interpret as mere belief.
2
Understand Ghazali's key refutation
Ghazali declares 'there is no proof for them in that.' Focus on his explanation that whenever 'iman' appears in these verses, it means faith combined with action — i.e., Islam.
3
Examine his supporting evidence
Ghazali provides two types of evidence: (1) hadith about the mustard seed of faith showing that sinners enter and then leave the Fire, and (2) Quranic verse on forgiveness (4:116) showing that sins other than shirk may be punished, meaning faith alone does not guarantee Paradise without deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَمَن يُؤْمِن بِرَبِّهِ فَلَا يَخافُ بَخْساً وَلَا رَهَقاً) ولقوله عز وجل : ( وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِاللَّهِ وَرُسُلِهِ أَوْلَئِكَ هُمُ الصِّدِّيقون) ولقوله تعالى : ( كُلَّمَا أُلْقِيَ فِيهَا فَوْجٌ سَأَلَهُمْ خَزَنَتُهَا إِلى قوله : ( وَقُلْنَا مَا نَزَّلَ اللهُ مِن شَيْءٍ ) . مكذباً . فَكَذَّبْنَا وقوله : « كلما ألقي فيها فوج ، عام ، فينبغي أن يكون من ألقي في النار ) ولقوله تعالى : ( لا يَصْلَاهَا إلا الأشقى الَّذِي كَذَّبَ وتَوَلَّى ) : وهذا حصر وإثبات ونفي ولقوله تعالى : مَن جَاءَ بِالْحَسَنَةِ فَلَهُ خَيْرٍ مِّنْهَا وَهُم مِن فَزَع يَوْمَئِذٍ آمِنُونَ فالإيمان رأس الحسنات ولقوله تعالى : ( وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُحْسِنِينَ ) وقال تعالى : ( إِنَّا لَا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ مَنْ أَحْسَنَ عَمَلًا ) ولا حجة لهم في ذلك ، فإنه حيث ذكر الإيمان في هذه الآيات أريد به الإيمان مع العمل ، إذ بينا ان الإيمان قد يطلق ويراد به الإسلام ، وهو الموافقة بالقلب والقول والعمل ودليل هذا التأويل أخبار كثيرة في معاقبة العاصين ومقادير العقاب ؛ وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان » . فكيف يخرج إذا لم يدخل . ومن القرآن ، قوله تعالى : إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ )
So whoever believes in his Lord will not fear injustice or oppression. And by His saying, Mighty and Majestic: (And those who believe in Allah and His messengers, they are the truthful ones). And by His saying, Most High: (Whenever a company is thrown into it, its keepers ask them... up to His saying: (And we say, 'Allah has not sent down anything'). Denying. So we denied. And His saying: 'Whenever a company is thrown into it, general, so it should be that whoever is thrown into the Fire...' And by His saying, Most High: (None will enter it except the most wretched one who denies and turns away): This is restriction, affirmation, and negation. And by His saying, Most High: (Whoever comes with a good deed will have better than it, and they will be safe from the terror of that Day) – so faith is the head of good deeds. And by His saying, Most High: (And Allah loves the doers of good). And He said, Most High: (Indeed, We do not waste the reward of whoever does good deeds). And there is no proof for them in that, because whenever faith is mentioned in these verses, what is meant is faith with action, since we have explained that faith may be used and what is meant is Islam, which is agreement with the heart, speech, and action. The evidence for this interpretation is many reports about the punishment of sinners and the degrees of punishment; and his saying, peace and blessings be upon him: 'He will come out of the Fire whoever has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith.' So how can he come out if he did not enter? And from the Quran, His saying, Most High: (Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills).
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Murji'ah sect. Ghazali begins by quoting a series of Quranic verses that the Murji'ah use as proof for their claim that faith alone (without works) is sufficient for salvation. The verses include: 1) 'Whoever believes in his Lord will not fear...' (Quran 72:13), 2) 'Those who believe in Allah and His messengers are the truthful' (Quran 57:19), 3) The description of the people of Hell asking for intercession (Quran 67:8-9), 4) 'None will enter it except the most wretched who denies and turns away' (Quran 92:15-16), 5) 'Whoever comes with a good deed will have better...' (Quran 27:89) – concluding that faith is the head of good deeds, 6) 'Allah loves the doers of good' (Quran 3:134), and 7) 'We do not waste the reward of whoever does good deeds' (Quran 18:30). After listing these, Ghazali declares: 'And there is no proof for them in that.' He explains that in all these verses, the term 'iman' (faith) is intended to mean faith combined with action (i.e., Islam), not mere belief. He had previously established that 'iman' can be used in a general sense to mean Islam, which includes inner conviction, verbal confession, and outward actions. Then he provides evidence for this interpretation: First, there are many traditions (akhbar) about the punishment of sinners and varying degrees of punishment in the afterlife. Second, the Prophet's hadith: 'He will come out of the Fire whoever has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith' – implying that such a person must first enter the Fire, otherwise how could he come out? Third, the Quranic verse: 'Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (Quran 4:116), which shows that sins other than shirk may be punished or forgiven by Allah's will, indicating that faith alone does not guarantee immediate Paradise without accountability for deeds.

Key Terms
الإيمان
العمل
المرجئة
الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith (iman) is only inner belief and does not require outward actions for salvation.
Correction: Ghazali shows that the Quranic verses Murji'ah use actually refer to 'iman with action' (Islam), and that hadith and Quran prove that faith without works leads to punishment.

Checkpoint
What is Ghazali's main argument against the Murji'ah in this passage?
A) The Murji'ah are correct that faith alone saves.
B) The Quranic verses they cite prove faith alone.
C) The word 'iman' in those verses means faith with action, not mere belief.
D) There is no punishment for believers.

Key Takeaway
Ghazali refutes the Murji'ah by showing that the Quranic term 'iman' in their proof-texts actually refers to faith accompanied by works, and that God's forgiveness and punishment depend on deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'None will enter it except the most wretched who denies and turns away', do you feel secure in your faith without examining your actions? What if your faith is merely a claim without the works that prove it?
?
The hadith says that even a mustard seed of faith will eventually bring a person out of the Fire – but only after entering it first. Does this thought make you examine the weight of your faith in your daily life, or do you assume that your declaration of faith guarantees immediate Paradise?
?
Ghazali insists that every mention of 'iman' in these verses means faith with actions. Consider your own life: if your faith were to be inspected as a combination of belief, speech, and action, would it still be called iman? What is one specific action you have neglected that you can commit to today as an expression of your faith?

The Murji'ah Argument from General Verses
Ghazali cites Murji'ah proof-texts and counters by redefining 'faith' as Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Murji'ah's use of general Quranic verses about reward does not prove that faith alone suffices, and how Ghazali counters by redefining 'faith' to include works.

Core Idea
General verses about reward do not automatically exclude works.

The Murji'ah school argued that faith alone, without works, guarantees salvation. They based this on Quranic verses that promise reward for believers in general terms. In this passage, Ghazali begins his refutation by showing that these verses actually refer to faith accompanied by works, i.e., Islam as a whole.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the verses Ghazali cites.
These are the verses the Murji'ah use as proof.
2
Identify the Murji'ah argument
The Murji'ah hold fast to the generalities of these verses. What do they conclude from them?
They conclude that faith alone is sufficient for reward.
3
Understand Ghazali's reinterpretation
Ghazali says 'faith' in these verses means faith with works, i.e., Islam. How does he justify this?
He refers to previous explanation that faith can be used to mean Islam.
4
Note the distinction
Distinguish between 'iman' (faith) and 'islam' (submission) in this context.
Islam includes heart, speech, and deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقوله تعالى : ( وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُحْسِنِينَ ) (۱) وقال تعالى : ( إِنَّا لَا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ مَنْ أَحْسَنَ عَمَلًا ) (٢) فهذه جملة من الآيات القرآنية الكريمة تمسك بعموماتها المرجئة . ولا حجة لهم في ذلك ، فإنه حيث ذكر الإيمان في هذه الآيات (۳) أريد به الإيمان مع العمل (٤) ، إذ بينا ان الإيمان قد يطلق ويراد به الإسلام ، وهو الموافقة بالقلب والقول والعمل . ودليل هذا التأويل (٥) أخبار كثيرة في معاقبة العاصين ومقادير العقاب (٦) ؛ وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان . فكيف يخرج إذا لم يدخل (۷) . ومن القرآن ، قوله تعالى : إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ ) (۸) والإستثناء بالمشيئة يدل على الإنقسام (۱) . وقوله تعالى : ( وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدِينَ فيها ) (۲) . وتخصيصه بالكفر تحكم . وقوله تعالى : ( ألا إِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ فِي عذابٍ مُقِيمٍ ) (۳) وقال تعالى : ( وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ ) (٤) فهذه العمومات في معارضة عموماتهم ، ولا بد من تسليط التخصيص والتأويل على الجانبين ، لأن الأخبار مصرحة بأن العصاة يعذبون (٦) ، بل قوله تعالى : ( وَإِن مِّنْكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ) (۷) كالصريح في أن ذلك لا بد منه للكل ، إذ لا يخلو مؤمن عن ذنب يرتكبه (۸)
And by His statement, the Exalted: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' (1), and He said, the Exalted: 'Indeed, We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds' (2). So this is a collection of noble Quranic verses by whose generalities the Murji'ah hold fast. And there is no proof for them in that, for verily, when faith is mentioned in these verses (3), what is meant is faith with works (4), since we have explained that 'faith' may be used and what is meant is Islam, which is agreement with the heart, speech, and deeds. And the proof of this interpretation (5) is many reports about the punishment of sinners and the measures of punishment (6); and his statement, peace be upon him: 'There will come out from the Fire he who has in his heart the weight of a speck of faith.' So how can he come out if he did not enter (7)? And from the Quran is His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (8). And the exception by will indicates division (1). And His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein' (2). And specifying it to disbelief is arbitrary. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, the wrongdoers are in an enduring punishment' (3). And He said, the Exalted: 'And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces will be cast down into the Fire' (4). So these generalities are in opposition to their generalities, and it is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly state that sinners are punished (6). Rather, His statement, the Exalted: 'And there is not one of you but will come to it' (7) is almost explicit that this is inevitable for all, since there is no believer free from a sin he commits (8).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Murji'ah position that faith alone (without works) is sufficient for salvation, using the general verses of the Quran. The author begins by citing two verses that the Murji'ah often cling to: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' and 'We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds.' He then states that these verses are a collection by which the Murji'ah hold fast to their generalities. However, he immediately denies that these provide proof for them, explaining that when 'faith' is mentioned in these verses, it means faith accompanied by works (the Islamic concept of iman as inner conviction plus outer actions). He references a previous explanation that the term 'faith' can be used to mean 'Islam'—agreement of heart, speech, and deeds. This is the first layer of refutation: the verses are interpreted in a way that includes works. Next, he provides evidence for this interpretation: there are many reports about the punishment of sinners and the degrees of punishment, including the hadith that those with even a speck of faith will eventually exit Hell. The argument is that if such sinners never entered Hell, how could they exit? Then he cites the Quranic verse: 'Allah forgives not that partners be associated with Him, but forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' The phrase 'for whom He wills' indicates a division—some are forgiven, some are not—implying that sinners can be punished. He then addresses another verse: 'Whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein.' He notes that restricting this verse only to disbelief is arbitrary. Similarly, verses about 'wrongdoers' and 'those who come with an evil deed are cast into the Fire' are general. So these generalities (about punishment) stand in opposition to the generalities the Murji'ah use (about reward). It is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly affirm that sinners are punished. Finally, he cites the verse 'There is not one of you but will come to it (the Fire),' which is nearly explicit that everyone must pass over Hell (on the Sirat), and no believer is free from sin. Thus, the Murji'ah argument is countered by other clear texts.

Key Terms
الإيمان
الإسلام
المرجئة
العمومات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Murji'ah think that general verses about reward prove faith alone is sufficient.
Correction: Ghazali shows these verses refer to faith with works, not faith alone.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, when faith is mentioned in the verses cited, what is meant?
A) Faith alone
B) Faith plus works (Islam)
C) Only inner conviction
D) Only outward actions

Key Takeaway
The Murji'ah's proof verses actually refer to faith that includes works, not faith alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about Allah's love for 'doers of good,' do you automatically assume you are included, or do you let the verse expose your shortcomings? What specific good deed have you neglected this week that you now realize is part of 'faith' itself?
?
Are there areas of your life where you rely on general promises of Allah's mercy while ignoring the specific conditions attached? Name one sin you have justified to yourself thinking, 'Faith alone is enough' — how does Ghazali's argument challenge that comfort?
?
The Murji'ah took verses out of context to build a theology that required little of them. In what ways do you take Quranic verses out of context to avoid personal change? Will you commit to reading the full context of a verse you've been using as an excuse?

Evidence for Punishment from Hadith and Quran
Ghazali provides hadith and Quranic evidence for punishment of sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key proofs Ghazali uses to show that believers who commit sins can be punished, including the hadith about exiting Hell and Quranic verses about punishment.

Core Idea
Believers can be punished for their sins; the hadith and Quran confirm this.

After establishing that the general verses about reward refer to faith with works, Ghazali now provides evidence that sinners among believers are indeed punished. He cites a well-known hadith and several Quranic verses that imply punishment for disobedience, even for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the hadith and verses.
2
Analyze the hadith
The hadith says people with a speck of faith will exit Hell. What does that imply about entry?
It implies they entered Hell first.
3
Examine the Quranic verses
The verses about shirk forgiveness, disobedience, wrongdoers, and evil deeds. How do they support punishment?
They show that even believers may face punishment.
4
Understand the refutation
Ghazali refutes the Murji'ah by showing that these verses cannot be restricted only to disbelievers.
Specifying them to disbelief is arbitrary.

And by His statement, the Exalted: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' (1), and He said, the Exalted: 'Indeed, We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds' (2). So this is a collection of noble Quranic verses by whose generalities the Murji'ah hold fast. And there is no proof for them in that, for verily, when faith is mentioned in these verses (3), what is meant is faith with works (4), since we have explained that 'faith' may be used and what is meant is Islam, which is agreement with the heart, speech, and deeds. And the proof of this interpretation (5) is many reports about the punishment of sinners and the measures of punishment (6); and his statement, peace be upon him: 'There will come out from the Fire he who has in his heart the weight of a speck of faith.' So how can he come out if he did not enter (7)? And from the Quran is His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (8). And the exception by will indicates division (1). And His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein' (2). And specifying it to disbelief is arbitrary. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, the wrongdoers are in an enduring punishment' (3). And He said, the Exalted: 'And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces will be cast down into the Fire' (4). So these generalities are in opposition to their generalities, and it is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly state that sinners are punished (6). Rather, His statement, the Exalted: 'And there is not one of you but will come to it' (7) is almost explicit that this is inevitable for all, since there is no believer free from a sin he commits (8).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Murji'ah position that faith alone (without works) is sufficient for salvation, using the general verses of the Quran. The author begins by citing two verses that the Murji'ah often cling to: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' and 'We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds.' He then states that these verses are a collection by which the Murji'ah hold fast to their generalities. However, he immediately denies that these provide proof for them, explaining that when 'faith' is mentioned in these verses, it means faith accompanied by works (the Islamic concept of iman as inner conviction plus outer actions). He references a previous explanation that the term 'faith' can be used to mean 'Islam'—agreement of heart, speech, and deeds. This is the first layer of refutation: the verses are interpreted in a way that includes works. Next, he provides evidence for this interpretation: there are many reports about the punishment of sinners and the degrees of punishment, including the hadith that those with even a speck of faith will eventually exit Hell. The argument is that if such sinners never entered Hell, how could they exit? Then he cites the Quranic verse: 'Allah forgives not that partners be associated with Him, but forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' The phrase 'for whom He wills' indicates a division—some are forgiven, some are not—implying that sinners can be punished. He then addresses another verse: 'Whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding eternally therein.' He notes that restricting this verse only to disbelief is arbitrary. Similarly, verses about 'wrongdoers' and 'those who come with an evil deed are cast into the Fire' are general. So these generalities (about punishment) stand in opposition to the generalities the Murji'ah use (about reward). It is necessary to apply specification and interpretation on both sides, because the reports explicitly affirm that sinners are punished. Finally, he cites the verse 'There is not one of you but will come to it (the Fire),' which is nearly explicit that everyone must pass over Hell (on the Sirat), and no believer is free from sin. Thus, the Murji'ah argument is countered by other clear texts.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If forgiveness of your lesser sins depends on 'whom He wills'—not on your mere avoidance of shirk—then what are you truly relying on for salvation? Does your daily life reflect trust in His mercy or presumption upon His pardon?
?
This passage forces you to accept that your disobedience, even as a believer, can lead to Hell. If you truly believed that tonight’s sin could land you in the Fire tomorrow, what would you change about your routine before you sleep tonight?

Balancing Generalities: The Necessity of Specification
Ghazali concludes by balancing general verses and citing universal passage through Fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why both sets of general verses (reward and punishment) require specification and interpretation, and how this refutes the Murji'ah position.

Core Idea
Neither reward nor punishment verses can be taken absolutely; both need specification.

Having presented verses that threaten punishment, Ghazali now confronts the Murji'ah's generalities with opposing generalities. He argues that the only consistent approach is to apply specification (takhsis) and interpretation (ta'wil) to both sides. The conclusive proof is that even the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Quran affirm that every soul will come to the Fire, meaning believers too.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the verses Ghazali introduces.
2
Understand the principle
Ghazali says both sets of generalities are in opposition. What must be done?
Specification and interpretation must be applied to both sides.
3
Examine the final proof
The verse 'There is not one of you but will come to it' supports universal accountability.
It implies everyone will face the Fire in some sense.
4
Connect to refutation
How does this dismantle the Murji'ah argument?
It shows that believers are not exempt from punishment; thus faith alone does not guarantee paradise without works.

ولقوله تعالى : ( وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُحْسِنِينَ ) (۱) وقال تعالى : ( إِنَّا لَا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ مَنْ أَحْسَنَ عَمَلًا ) (٢) فهذه جملة من الآيات القرآنية الكريمة تمسك بعموماتها المرجئة . ولا حجة لهم في ذلك ، فإنه حيث ذكر الإيمان في هذه الآيات (۳) أريد به الإيمان مع العمل (٤) ، إذ بينا ان الإيمان قد يطلق ويراد به الإسلام ، وهو الموافقة بالقلب والقول والعمل . ودليل هذا التأويل (٥) أخبار كثيرة في معاقبة العاصين ومقادير العقاب (٦) ؛ وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان . فكيف يخرج إذا لم يدخل (۷) . ومن القرآن ، قوله تعالى : إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَنْ يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ ) (۸) والإستثناء بالمشيئة يدل على الإنقسام (۱) . وقوله تعالى : ( وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدِينَ فيها ) (۲) . وتخصيصه بالكفر تحكم . وقوله تعالى : ( ألا إِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ فِي عذابٍ مُقِيمٍ ) (۳) وقال تعالى : ( وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ ) (٤) فهذه العمومات في معارضة عموماتهم ، ولا بد من تسليط التخصيص والتأويل على الجانبين ، لأن الأخبار مصرحة بأن العصاة يعذبون (٦) ، بل قوله تعالى : ( وَإِن مِّنْكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ) (۷) كالصريح في أن ذلك لا بد منه للكل ، إذ لا يخلو مؤمن عن ذنب يرتكبه (۸)
And by His statement, the Exalted: 'And Allah loves the doers of good' (1), and He said, the Exalted: 'Indeed, We do not waste the reward of those who do good deeds' (2). So this is a collection of noble Quranic verses by whose generalities the Murji'ah hold fast. And there is no proof for them in that, for verily, when faith is mentioned in these verses (3), what is meant is faith with works (4), since we have explained that 'faith' may be used and what is meant is Islam, which is agreement with the heart, speech, and deeds. And the proof of this interpretation (5) is many reports about the punishment of sinners and the measures of punishment (6); and his statement, peace be upon him: 'There will come out from the Fire he who has in his heart the weight of a speck of faith.' So how can he come out if he did not enter (7)? And from the Quran is His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (8). The Necessary Specification of Punishment Verses and the Fate of Believers
Ghazali argues for the necessary specification of punishment verses and concludes that believers are not eternally punished.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why general punishment verses must be specified and interpreted, and how this leads to the conclusion that believers who die on tawhid are not eternally punished.

Core Idea
General punishment verses require specification to avoid contradiction; believers are not eternally punished.

Imam Ghazali addresses a critical theological question: do the Qur'anic verses that threaten eternal punishment apply to all sinners, including believers? In this passage, he argues that such general verses must be interpreted in light of other evidence, and he establishes the orthodox position that while disbelievers face eternal punishment, believers who die upon tawhid are ultimately saved, regardless of their sins.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement about exception by will
Understand that the exception 'illa ma sha'a Allah' indicates a division among sinners.
2
Examine the general punishment verses cited
Notice the verses that seem to promise eternal punishment for all disobedience.
3
Grasp the necessity of specification and interpretation
See why Ghazali insists these must be applied to both sides of apparently conflicting verses.
4
Discern the distinction between disbelief and lesser sins
Learn that shirk is unforgivable, but other sins may be forgiven, and the conclusion that monotheists are not eternally punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإستثناء بالمشيئة يدل على الإنقسام (۱) . وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ خَالِدِينَ فيها ) (٢) . وتخصيصه بالكفر تحكم . وقوله تعالى : ( ألا إِنَّ الظَّالِمِينَ فِي عذابٍ مُقِيمٍ (٣) ﴾ وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ (٤) فهذه العمومات في معارضة عموماتهم ، ولا بد من تسليط التخصيص والتأويل على الجانبين ، لأن الأخبار مصرحة بأن العصاة يعذبون (٦) ، بل قوله تعالى : ( وَإِن مِّنْكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا ) (۷) كالصريح في أن ذلك لا بد منه للكل ، إذ لا يخلو مؤمن عن ذنب يرتكبه(۸) من جحد نبوة الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم مثلا فهو كافر ، ولو لم يجعل مع الله إلها آخر ، والمغفرة منتفية عنه بلا خلاف . ويعفر ما دون الشرك تحت إمكان المغفرة ، فمن مات على التوحيد غير مخلد في النار وان ارتكب من الكبائر غير الشرط ما عساه أن يرتكب .
And the exception by the will indicates division. And His statement, the Exalted: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the Fire of Hell, abiding therein forever.' And specifying it to disbelief is arbitrary. And His statement, the Exalted: 'Indeed, the wrongdoers are in a lasting punishment.' And He said, the Exalted: 'And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces will be thrown into the Fire.' So these general verses are in opposition to their general verses, and it is necessary to apply specification and interpretation to both sides, because the reports clearly state that sinners are punished. Rather, His statement, the Exalted: 'And there is none of you except that he will pass over it' is almost explicit that this is necessary for all, since no believer is free from a sin he commits. Whoever denies the prophethood of the Messenger, for example, is a disbeliever, even if he does not take another god with Allah, and forgiveness is excluded from him without dispute. And what is less than shirk falls under the possibility of forgiveness. So whoever dies upon tawhid will not be eternally in the Fire, even if he commits of the major sins besides shirk as much as he may commit.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the interpretation of verses threatening punishment for sin. The author begins by stating that the exception by the will indicates a division of sins into major and minor. He then cites several general verses warning of punishment for disobedience, wrongdoing, and evil deeds. These verses, he argues, stand in opposition to the general verses of the Mu'tazila that promise forgiveness. Therefore, both sets of verses must be subjected to specification (takhsīṣ) and interpretation (taʼwīl), because the reports clearly affirm that sinners will be punished. The key verse 'There is none of you except that he will pass over it' (Q. 19:71) is taken as nearly explicit that everyone must experience this passing, since no believer is sinless. The author then clarifies that one who denies prophethood is a disbeliever, even without shirk, and forgiveness is not for him. In contrast, sins less than shirk remain under the possibility of forgiveness. The conclusion: whoever dies upon tawḥīd will not be eternally in the Fire, even if they committed major sins other than shirk. This establishes the orthodox position that believers are not eternally punished.

Correction: The verse refers to passing over the bridge (ṣirāṭ) above Hell, not entering it. Ghazali uses it to show that all people will experience this passing, not that they will be cast into the Fire.

Proof that Believers Are Not Eternally Punished
Ghazali cites Quranic verses and hadith to argue that believers are not eternally punished for sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ghazali uses Quranic verses and hadith to prove that a believer who commits major sins will not remain in Hell forever.

Core Idea
Eternal punishment for believers is not literal; other verses specify it away.

In this passage, Ghazali tackles a critical theological question: do believers who die in sin suffer eternal punishment? He begins by citing verses that seem to threaten everlasting fire, but then immediately shows how they are qualified by other divine texts. You will see how the Quran and hadith together preserve the hope of ultimate salvation for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without translation. Let the rhythm and key terms (like 'إيمان', 'شرك', 'مشيئة') sink in.
The passage is dense with Quranic references.
2
Study the translation and commentary
Read the English translation and then the teacher commentary. Notice how Ghazali argues that general verses are 'specified' by other verses.
3
Analyze the specifying verses
Identify the verses that threaten eternal punishment and the verses that limit them (e.g., 4:48, the hadith about the mustard seed). Ask: what is the rule for interpreting such apparent contradictions?
This is the core of Ghazali's method.
4
Understand the implication
Reflect on the theological conclusion: no believer, no matter how sinful, will be eternally punished. How does this uphold both God's justice and mercy?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال : ﴿ ثُمَّ نُنَجِّي الَّذِينَ اتَّقَواْ ﴾
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَنَ يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ فَإِنَّ لَهُ نَارَ جَهَنَّمَ ﴾
وكل آية ذكر الله عز وجل العمل الصالح فيها مقروناً بالإيمان
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُتَعَمِّداً فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِداً فِيهَا ﴾
وهذه العمومات أيضاً مخصوصة ، بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾
فينبغي أن تبقى له مشيئة في مغفرة ما سوى الشرك
وكذلك قوله عليه السلام : « يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من إيمان »
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّا لا نُضِيعُ أَجْرَ مَنْ أَحْسَنَ عَمَلاً ﴾
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ لا يُضِيعُ أَجْرَ الْمُحْسِنِينَ ﴾ فكيف يضيع أجر أصل الإيمان وجميع الطاعات بمعصية واحدة
وقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَمَنْ يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِناً مُتَعَمِّداً ﴾ أي لإيمانه وقد ورد على مثل هذا السبب
Then He said: "Then We save those who fear" and His saying: "And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the fire of Hell." And every verse in which Allah Almighty mentions righteous deeds coupled with faith. And His saying: "And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein." And these generalities are also specified, by the evidence of His saying: "And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills." So it must be that He has will in forgiving what is other than shirk. Also His (peace be upon him) saying: "There will come out of the Fire whoever has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith." And His saying: "Indeed, We do not waste the reward of those who do good." And His saying: "Indeed, Allah does not waste the reward of the doers of good." So how could He waste the reward of the foundation of faith and all acts of obedience due to one sin? And His saying: "And whoever kills a believer intentionally" means on account of his faith, and it has been revealed on such an occasion.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran and hadith that a believer who commits major sins is not eternally punished. Ghazali cites several verses that seem to threaten eternal punishment, but argues they are specified by other texts. He begins with verses about saving the God-fearing and threatening the disobedient. Then he mentions the verse about killing a believer intentionally, which seems to promise eternal Hell. He argues that these general verses are specified by the verse 'He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (4:48), leaving room for God's will to forgive any sin less than shirk. He then cites the hadith about the mustard seed of faith ensuring eventual exit from Hell. He adds verses about God not wasting reward, arguing that it would be inconsistent to waste the reward of faith and all good deeds because of one sin. Finally, he interprets the verse about killing a believer as being revealed on a specific occasion (i.e., it refers to killing because of faith), thus it does not apply generally.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses threatening eternal punishment for sinners are taken literally without exception.
Correction: This passage shows they are specified by other texts; thus a believer who dies in sin is not eternally punished.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, why does the verse 'Whoever kills a believer intentionally' not imply eternal punishment for such a killer if he is a believer?
A) Because the killer is not a believer.
B) Because the verse was revealed concerning killing because of faith.
C) Because God always forgives murder.
D) Because the verse is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
A believer's sins do not negate the reward of faith; God's mercy and the intercession of faith ensure eventual salvation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you feel that all your good deeds are lost? Are you living under the weight of your failures rather than the hope of God's mercy? What would it take for you to truly believe that your faith matters more than your shortcomings?
?
Ghazali argues that the reward of faith and all acts of obedience cannot be wasted by one sin. Does your life reflect that conviction? What specific sin are you holding onto that contradicts this truth? How will you repent and trust that God's will to forgive includes you?
?
The hadith says that even a mustard seed of faith will eventually bring you out of Hell. Are you confident that you have that seed? What are you doing to nurture it? Or do you take it for granted? When you sin, do you immediately turn back to Allah, or do you despair?
